ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
§§ 14-1—14-10 RESERVED.
ARTICLE II. WASTE MANAGEMENT FACILITIES
DIVISION 1. GENERALLY
§ 14-11 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the terms or words used herein shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in the Virginia Waste Management Act, VA Code §§
10.1-1400 through 10.1-1457.
(Prior Code, § 14-11) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
Cross-reference:
   Definitions and rules of construction generally, see §
1-2
§ 14-12 PURPOSE OF ARTICLE.
   This article is established for the purpose of protecting, promoting and
preserving an environment that is conducive to public health and welfare,
preventing the creation of nuisances, and the depletion of natural resources
and to maintain such levels of air quality and water quality as will protect
human health, welfare and safety, and to the greatest degree practicable,
prevent injury to plant and animal life, and property and to nurture the
comfort of the people in their enjoyment of life and property, and to encourage
the social and economic development of the county and to facilitate the
enjoyment of its attractions.
(Prior Code, § 14-12) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-13 ARTICLE DOES NOT AFFECT ZONING AND SUBDIVISION ORDINANCES,
COMPREHENSIVE PLAN OR OTHER REGULATIONS.
   (A)   This article shall not operate to alter, modify or rescind any
existing zoning or subdivision ordinances, or to affect the application and
enforceability of the county’s comprehensive plan.
   (B)   Nothing in this article shall be construed to exempt any person or
applicant from any other federal, state or local regulations pertaining to the
establishment, operation or maintenance of a solid waste management facility.
Other such regulations include, but shall not be limited to, the National
Fishing Enhancement Act of 1984, being 33 U.S.C. §§ 2101 et seq., the Clean
Water Act, the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969, being 42 U.S.C. §§
4321 et seq., the Fish and Wildlife Act of 1956, being 16 U.S.C. §§ 742a et
seq., the Federal Power Act of 1920, being 16 U.S.C. Chapter 12, the Historic
Preservation Act of 1966, being U.S.C. §§ 300101 et seq,, the Endangered
Species Act, being 16 U.S.C. §§ 1531 et seq., and the Virginia Waste Management
Act, being VA Code 10.1, Chapter 14, Articles 1 through 8.
(Prior Code, § 14-13) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-14 VIOLATIONS OF ARTICLE.
   Unless otherwise specifically provided, a violation of any provision of this
article shall constitute a Class 1 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-14) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-15 RESPONSIBILITY OF ADMINISTRATOR TO ENFORCE ARTICLE.
   The County Administrator shall be responsible for enforcing the provisions
of this article.
(Prior Code, § 14-15) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-16 ENFORCEMENT OF ARTICLE BY SUIT FOR INJUNCTIVE RELIEF.
   The provisions of this article may be enforced by a suit for injunctive
relief in a court of competent jurisdiction.
(Prior Code, § 14-16) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-17 EXEMPTIONS FROM ARTICLE.
   Facilities for the disposal of solid waste from the extraction,
beneficiation and processing of oils and minerals, including coal, shall be
exempt from this article; provided such facilities are managed in accordance
with the requirements promulgated by the appropriate agencies of the
commonwealth. Such exemption shall not apply to facilities for the disposal of
by-products of coal combustion, such as fly ash and bottom ash.
(Prior Code, § 14-17) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-18 APPLICATION OF DIVISIONS 2 AND 3 OF ARTICLE.
   (A)   The provisions of Divisions 2 and 3 of this article shall apply to
landfills operated by the county or by a regional waste or service authority in
which the county is a participating member. In addition, such provisions shall
apply to captive industrial landfills which accept waste only from a business
or industry located on the same site.
   (B)   The provisions of Divisions 2 and 3 of this article shall not apply to
privately-owned or privately-operated solid waste management facilities, other
than captive industrial landfills; provided, however, that such provisions
shall apply to privately-owned or privately-operated solid waste management
facilities, in the event the prohibition provisions of §
14-19 are ruled invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction.
(Prior Code, § 14-18) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-19 PRIVATE FACILITIES PROHIBITED.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to establish, maintain or operate an
unregulated dumping place, an open dump, or a privately-owned or privately-
operated solid waste management facility within the territorial boundaries of
the county.
(Prior Code, § 14-19) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-20 RIGHT TO INSPECT AND CLOSE FACILITY.
   (A)   The Board of Supervisors reserves the right to make such inspections
of the site of a solid waste management facility as necessary to carry out the
purposes of this article. The Board also reserves the right to suspend and
close a facility upon a finding by the Board of imminent dangers to the public
or to the environment.
   (B)   The Board shall provide a reason for such closing to the facility
manager and owner and a list of actions to be taken to correct the problems.
(Prior Code, § 14-20) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-21 TRANSPORTATION OF SOLID WASTE.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to transport for disposal into the
county any garbage, trash or refuse which has been compacted or baled in such a
manner that it cannot be readily examined and inspected by manual means by
county officials for the purpose of determining whether such garbage, trash or
refuse contains hazardous substances.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to collect, haul, transport or
convey garbage or trash for disposal within the county, except from one’s own
residence to an approved bulk container in the community or to a county-
approved solid waste management facility.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person to transport refuse to points
through and outside the county, except for the transporting of refuse in
adequately covered trucks to points outside of the county.
(Prior Code, § 14-21) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§§ 14-22—14-26 RESERVED.
DIVISION 2. SITING REQUIREMENTS
§ 14-27 IN AREAS OF BASE FLOODS.
   A solid waste management facility shall not be sited or constructed in areas
subject to base floods.
(Prior Code, § 14-27) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-28 IN GEOLOGICALLY UNSTABLE AREAS.
   No solid waste management facility shall be sited in geologically unstable
areas where adequate foundation support for the construction components for the
facility does not exist, giving due consideration to soil conditions,
geological and geomorphologic features, human-made features, caverns, tunnels,
mines and sinkholes.
(Prior Code, § 14-28) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-29 LOCATION OF DISPOSAL AREA WITH RESPECT TO FLOWING WATER, DRINKING WATER
SOURCES, ROADS, RESIDENCES, SCHOOLS AND THE LIKE.
   (A)   No solid waste management facility disposal area shall be closer than
500 feet from any regular flowing surface body of water or 1,000 feet from any
well, spring or other groundwater source of drinking water.
   (B)   Any solid waste management facility disposal area shall also be a
minimum of 100 feet from any public road or right-of-way used by persons other
than the person operating the facility, and a minimum of 1,500 feet from any
residence, school, hospital, nursing home, church, recreational or park area,
or retail establishment.
(Prior Code, § 14-29) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-30 SEPARATION OF DISPOSAL AREA FROM MAXIMUM SEASONAL WATER TABLE.
   There shall be a minimum separation of ten feet between the deposit of solid
waste and the maximum seasonal water table or bedrock, unless equal isolation
or separation can be achieved and maintained by engineered construction and
operation methods to meet the standards of the State Department of Waste
Management.
(Prior Code, § 14-30) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-31 ACCESS FROM PRIMARY HIGHWAY.
   The access from a primary highway to a solid waste management facility site
shall be an all-weather paved road.
(Prior Code, § 14-31) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-32 REVIEW BY PLANNING COMMISSION.
   The siting of a solid waste management facility shall be subject to review
by the Planning Commission pursuant to VA Code Title 15.2, Chapter 9, Article
II.
(Prior Code, § 14-32) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§§ 14-33—14-37 RESERVED.
DIVISION 3. CERTIFICATE
§ 14-38 REQUIRED.
   No person shall establish, operate or maintain a solid waste management
facility without a certificate from the Board of Supervisors.
(Prior Code, § 14-38) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
Statutory reference:
   Local certificate prerequisite to issuance of state permit, see VA Code §
10.1-1408.1
§ 14-39 APPLICATION GENERALLY.
   (A)   An application for a certificate required by this division shall
contain the following information:
      (1)   The name, address and phone number of the applicant;
      (2)   The names, addresses, and work and home phone numbers of all
persons and entities owning an interest exceeding 5%, whether expressed or
silent, in the proposed solid waste management facility’s operating entity, in
the site or in the applicant;
      (3)   The legal description of the property on which the facility is
proposed to be located and a tax map reference;
      (4)   A copy of the lease or deed establishing the applicant’s right to
use the proposed site;
      (5)   A description of the current use of the proposed site;
      (6)   The present zoning district of the site;
      (7)   The proposed size and type of solid waste management facility;
      (8)   A preliminary site plan showing the boundary of the site, the
proposed disposal areas and other facilities and equipment to be located at the
site;
      (9)   A list of all property owners, both surface and mineral, and
mailing addresses, as shown on the county land books, who are contiguous,
adjacent or within one mile of the proposed site;
      (10)   The names, addresses and phone numbers of all residents and owners
living within a one-mile radius of the proposed solid waste management facility
site, and detailed information regarding the source of each listed resident’s
water supply and any surface and water damage reported to the applicant by the
resident due to past or present mining activities. The applicant shall take a
written statement from the resident and have the resident sign and verify that
the information contained therein is true and accurate, with a copy being given
to the resident. Should the resident refuse to cooperate with the applicant,
the applicant shall report that fact in the application;
      (11)   A description of the type of waste to be deposited in the proposed
solid waste management facility;
      (12)   A description of the anticipated rates or fees to be charged for
the disposal of solid waste, an estimate of the total volume of waste to be
disposed of each year and an estimate of the total annual revenues to be
generated by waste disposal activities at the proposed site;
      (13)   A complete description of the nature of any contracts and the
identity of parties to contracts for the acceptance of solid waste involving
the proposed site that have been agreed to at the time the application is
submitted or prior to the final action of the Board of Supervisors or its agent
on the application;
      (14)   A complete and thorough listing concerning the environmental
record of the entities who have been in contact or have contracted with the
applicant to utilize the solid waste management facility;
      (15)   A complete and thorough record of the compliance history of the
applicant concerning state and federal environmental laws;
      (16)   All information contained in subsections (A)(12), (A)(13), (A)(14)
and (A)(15) above shall be updated periodically by the applicant pending the
approval or disapproval of the application;
      (17)   A plan for land use of the site after the facility is closed;
      (18)   Complete information regarding violations of federal or state
environmental laws or regulations by any of the applicant’s owners, officers,
or any corporate entities in which the applicant owns or has owned an interest.
The environmental controls referred to herein include, but are not limited to,
any and all statutes and regulations enforced by the State Division of Mine,
Land and Reclamation, the State Division of Mines and Quarries, the State
Department of Mines, Minerals and Energy, the State Office of Surface Mining,
the State Air Pollution Control Board, the State Water Control Board, and the
U.S. Army Corps of Engineers;
      (19)   Information regarding felony convictions of the applicant or any
of the applicant’s owners, officers or any corporate entities in which the
applicant, or any of its owners, owns or has owned an interest;
      (20)   A map showing the location of the facility, the roads and rights-
of-way giving access to the facility, and an approximate location of
residences, schools, hospitals, churches and retail establishments located
along any street or secondary road proposed to be used as an access road for
the facility;
      (21)   A site plan showing the entire acreage owned or controlled by the
applicant, the names of adjoining property owners, the location of any
adjoining property or other properties within 1,500 feet of the site, and the
location of any residence, school, hospital, church, recreational park or
retail establishment;
      (22)   The anticipated type, amount and source of financial protection to
be provided by the applicant to satisfy the financial assurance regulations of
State Department of Waste Management;
      (23)   The names, addresses and relevant experience of all key personnel
to be employed or retained by the applicant in connection with the operation of
the proposed solid waste management facility; and
      (24)   Complete information regarding violations of federal or state
environmental laws or regulations by any of the key personnel identified in
subsection (A)(23) above or in any application submitted to the State
Department of Waste Management.
   (B)   The application shall be sworn to as being complete and accurate and
shall be signed by the president of the applicant’s corporation, if the
applicant is a corporation; by all of the partners if a partnership, both
general and silent partners; or the individual sole proprietor, if same
applies.
(Prior Code, § 14-39) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-40 PLANS, TEST SAMPLES AND THE LIKE MAY BE REQUESTED FROM APPLICANT.
   (A)   In addition to the information required by §
14-39, the applicant for a certificate may be requested to furnish engineering
and site plans to show:
      (1)   The slope and direction of rock strata and aquifers;
      (2)   The availability of cover material on the site or arrangements for
obtaining adequate cover material from a borrow site;
      (3)   The location of springs, seeps and other groundwater sources, and
other possible groundwater intrusion to the site;
      (4)   The location of any gas, water, sewage, electrical or other
transmission lines under, on or over the site;
      (5)   The prior existence of any such facilities on the site; and
      (6)   The location on the site of any prior open dump, landfill, lagoon,
surface or deep mine or similar facility.
   (B)   If requested, the applicant shall provide detailed core hole samples
from two locations within 50 horizontal feet of the opposite extremities of the
site of at least 300 feet deep (50 feet deep if near a utilized freshwater
aquifer). If requested, the applicant shall also provide certified test results
of the water quality of any freshwater aquifers beneath the proposed site to a
depth of 300 feet. The applicant may be asked to furnish a plan for
transporting waste through the county to the waste management facility site.
(Prior Code, § 14-40) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-41 ADDITIONAL INFORMATION TO BE FURNISHED BY APPLICANT IF FACILITY IS NEAR
MINING OPERATION.
   If the applicant’s proposed solid waste management facility is situated
within 3,000 feet of any abandoned, inactive or active coal mining operation,
the following information shall be supplied as part of the application prior to
consideration of the applicant’s request for siting approval:
   (A)   The names and addresses of the coal and mineral owners within a 3,000-
foot radius of the proposed solid waste management facility site, with
supporting documentation as available in the county land book records;
   (B)   A list, with certification from the Division of Mined Land Reclamation
of the State Department of Mines, Minerals and Energy, of all applications and
past and present permits for the surface mining or deep mining of coal within a
3,000-foot radius of the proposed solid waste management facility site;
   (C)   If the Division of Mined Land Reclamation finds that such permit
applications are pending or such mining is in progress or that abandoned coal
mines exist within the 3,000-foot radius area, the applicant shall provide
copies of the relevant mining permit applications, complete with maps of the
active, inactive, proposed or abandoned mining sites, with the boundary of the
proposed solid waste management facility site outlined in red and the
boundaries of the proposed, active, inactive or abandoned mining site outlined
in blue; and the applicant shall also supply copies of all relevant
hydrological formation and subsidence control plans contained within the mining
permit applications as set forth in the mining permit files; and
   (D)   If the landfill site is on limestone or similar soluble rock, it will
be required that the applicant document all caves, openings, sinkholes,
disappearing streams, known cave passages and any types of subterranean life
forms and their status on the federal and state endangered species list.
(Prior Code, § 14-41) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-42 FEE.
   The non-refundable fee to cover the costs of processing and reviewing an
application under this division, giving notice to affected property owners and
advertising a public hearing shall be a minimum of $5,000 or the actual cost of
processing and reviewing the application, whichever is greater, and shall
include the costs of legal and technical review. The minimum fee shall be
payable by the applicant at the time the application is submitted.
(Prior Code, § 14-42) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-43 SUBMISSION OF APPLICATION ESTABLISHES NO RIGHT.
   The submission of an application pursuant to this division shall not result
in the establishment of any right to establish, operate or maintain a solid
waste management facility.
(Prior Code, § 14-43) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-44 RETURN OF APPLICATION TO APPLICANT.
   If the Board of Supervisors or its agent returns an application submitted
under this division to the applicant with instructions to provide additional
information, because of the applicant’s failure to obtain approval required by
any ordinance of the county or the Code of Virginia, or because of the
application of this article or any other ordinance prohibiting the
establishment, operation or maintenance of a privately-owned or privately-
operated solid waste management facility, the application shall be deemed
incomplete and no further action by the Board or its agent shall be required
until the reason for the return of the application has been corrected. Should
any application be so returned, the applicant shall have the right to resubmit
the application to be reviewed by the Board or its agent for completeness
without the deposit of any additional application fee.
(Prior Code, § 14-44) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-45 HEARING ON APPLICATION; ISSUANCE OR DENIAL GENERALLY.
   (A)   Within 60 days after the receipt of a complete application for a
certificate under this division, as determined by the Board of Supervisors or
its agent, the Board shall hold a public hearing on the proposed siting of the
solid waste management facility. The hearing shall be advertised as non-revenue
ordinances are advertised. The Board shall make a decision following the public
hearing no later than 120 days following the receipt of the complete
application. If the Board approves the siting location, it shall issue the
certificate. If the Board declines to issue the certificate, it shall advise
the applicant of the reasons for declining.
   (B)   In denying a certificate, the Board of Supervisors may state
conditions which, if complied with, would result in the issuance of a
certificate, and if the applicant agrees to comply with such conditions and
resubmits his or her application containing all such conditions, the Board may
grant a certificate upon further public hearing.
(Prior Code, § 14-45) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-46 CRITERIA FOR ISSUANCE.
   (A)   In making a decision as to whether the certificate shall be issued
under this division, the Board of Supervisors shall consider the potential
affect of the proposed solid waste management facility on the health, safety
and welfare of the county and its residents, and the criteria set forth in this
division. The Board, in determining whether to issue a certificate, may also
consider whether the proposed facility is compatible to existing land uses and
what visual barriers, such as tree buffers or berms, are to screen the site
from adjacent residences, schools, hospitals, churches, parks and recreation
areas, and retail establishments. The Board may consider litter on the access
road to the site, fugitive dust, noise, odor, hours of operation and artificial
lighting that may negatively affect adjacent uses of land.
   (B)   The Board of Supervisors shall also consider the following siting
criteria in evaluating an application for a certificate under this division:
      (1)   Suitability of the proposed solid waste management facility site in
light of the surface and subsurface conditions (porous, fractured or subsided,
or is subjected to same from past, present or future mining, or as otherwise
affected by natural sink holes, fissures and cracks);
      (2)   Impact of the proposed solid waste management facility site on
groundwater and water used by surface owners and localities within the county;
      (3)   The fitness of the applicant, its owners and their companies, to
guard and to protect the safety and welfare of the public and of water and
other natural resources;
      (4)   The likelihood that a breach of the solid waste management facility
containment systems could occur, and if so, the impact such a breach would have
upon groundwater and surface water; and
      (5)   The impact of the solid waste management facility and its operation
upon surrounding property values.
   (C)   No certificate shall be issued under this division, if the Board of
Supervisors determines that the applicant lacks sufficient financial resources
to safely and adequately establish, operate, maintain and close the proposed
facility.
   (D)   No certificate shall be issued under this division, if the Board of
Supervisors determines that the applicant, its owners, officers, any corporate
entities in which the applicant owns or has owned an interest, or any key
personnel identified in the application or any application submitted to the
Virginia Department of Waste Management have been found to have violated any
federal or state environmental laws or regulations.
(Prior Code, § 14-46) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-47 CONTENTS.
   (A)   If a certificate is granted under this division, the certificate shall
name the applicant, its address, describe in detail the location of the site,
and list the types of solid waste which may be disposed of on the site. The
certificate shall specifically refer to the date of the application and
specifically list the date of any amendments thereto.
   (B)   The certificate shall state that the location and operation of the
facility are consistent with all applicable ordinances of the county. A copy of
the application and all amendments thereto shall be attached to the copy of the
certificate which is to be filed by the applicant with the Virginia Department
of Waste Management.
(Prior Code, § 14-47) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-48 NOT TRANSFERRABLE.
   No certificate issued pursuant to this division shall be transferrable or
assignable. A material change in the corporate ownership of any corporation
that has been issued a certificate shall be considered a prohibited transfer.
(Prior Code, § 14-48) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-49 CHANGES IN SITE, OPERATIONS AND THE LIKE AFTER ISSUANCE.
   Once a certificate has been issued pursuant to this division, the size of
the site shall not be enlarged, nor the type of waste accepted changed, without
reapplication and a new public hearing. A site may be decreased in size or the
types of waste or volume disposed of may be reduced without amendment of a
certificate or the submission of new application; provided, that in the event
of a reduction in the size of the site or reduction in types of waste to be
handled at any time after the issuance of the certificate, the applicant shall,
within 30 days thereof, file with the Board of Supervisors a new plat of the
site and a new description of the types of waste which will be disposed of at
the site. A new certificate shall be required pursuant to this division for the
establishment of a new facility, the expansion of any existing facility or any
material change in design or process at an existing facility.
(Prior Code, § 14-49) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-50 LAPSE.
   A certificate issued pursuant to this division shall lapse 12 months after
the final action of the Board of Supervisors on the application, unless the
holder of the certificate has begun the actual construction of the proposed
facility. A certificate granted pursuant to this division shall lapse if, at
any time, the holder of the certificate ceases operation of the facility for a
period of 12 months.
(Prior Code, § 14-50) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§ 14-51 REVOCATION.
   A certificate granted pursuant to this division may be revoked by the Board
of Supervisors, if the Board determines that the facility is being operated or
maintained in a manner that poses a substantial present or potential hazard to
human health or the environment. A certificate may also be revoked by the
Board, if the Board determines that the grant of the certificate was based on
an application containing material misrepresentations or omissions.
(Prior Code, § 14-51) (Ord. passed 11-9-1990)
§§ 14-52—14-56 RESERVED.
ARTICLE III. LITTER CONTROL AND WASTE DISPOSAL
§ 14-57 ARTICLE TITLE.
   This article shall be known and may be cited as the “Litter Control and
Solid Waste Disposal Ordinance.”
(Prior Code, § 14-57) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-58 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ANTIQUE MOTOR VEHICLE. A motor vehicle which was actually manufactured, or
designated by the manufacturer as a model manufactured in a calendar year not
less than 25 years prior to January 1 of each calendar year and is owned solely
as a collector’s item, and is used for participation in club activities,
exhibits, tours, parades and similar uses, but in no event used for
transportation.
   BRUSH. Bushes, branches, briars, leaves and similar material.
   BULK WASTE. All waste materials, including, but not limited to, junked
furniture and large appliances, stoves, fence wire, scrap metal, transmissions,
rear ends and other items which are of a nature which would tend to impede the
collection process or damage collection or compaction equipment.
   BULK WASTE CONTAINER. Any container or area designated for the deposit of
bulky items only, including, but not limited to, junked furniture and
appliances, stoves, fence wire and scrap metal, and other bulky waste.
   COMMERCIAL SOLID WASTE. Garbage, rubbish and trash resulting from the normal
operations of commercial establishments.
   CONTAINER. A receptacle which is not less than two cubic yards in capacity
and is constructed of such quality as to maintain the original shape when
placed at an outdoor location and is reasonably resistant to rust and
corrosion.
   COUNTY CONTAINER. A container placed and maintained by the county or its
agents for use by individuals.
   COUNTY GOVERNMENTAL SOLID WASTE. Garbage, rubbish and trash resulting from
the normal activities of the county government, excluding solid waste resulting
from the activities of the school system.
   GARBAGE. Animal, vegetable or mineral matter derived from the preparation or
packaging of foodstuffs.
   HOUSEHOLD SOLID WASTE. Garbage, rubbish and trash resulting from the normal
day-to-day activities of households.
   INSTITUTION. Any public or private establishment which educates, instructs,
treats for health purposes, or otherwise performs a service or need for the
community, region, state or nation, excluding the county school system.
   INSTITUTION SOLID WASTE. Garbage, rubbish and trash resulting from the
operations of institutions.
   LITTER. All waste materials including, but not limited to, bottles, glass,
crockery, cans, scrap metal, paper, plastic, rubber, garbage, offal, waste or
scrap building materials, tires, brush, junked furniture and appliances,
carcasses, disposable packages, or containers, which are thrown or disposed of
as prohibited herein, but not including the properly disposed of waste of the
primary processes of mining, logging, saw-milling, farming or manufacturing.
   LITTER RECEPTACLE. A container with a capacity of not less than ten gallons,
constructed of such quality as to maintain the original shape when placed at an
outdoor location, reasonably resistant to rust and corrosion, and placed for
use as a depository for litter.
   MOTOR VEHICLE. Every vehicle which is self-propelled or designed for self-
propulsion. A structure designed, used or maintained primarily to be loaded on
or affixed to a MOTOR VEHICLE to provide a mobile dwelling, sleeping place,
office or commercial space shall be considered a part of a MOTOR VEHICLE.
   PERMITTED DISPOSAL SITE. A location approved by the proper agencies of the
state and the county for the disposal of waste.
   PRIVATE CONTAINER. A container placed and maintained for use by a commercial
business or institution or its agents.
   PRIVATE PROPERTY. Property owned by any person, including, but not limited
to, yards, grounds, driveways, entranceways, passageways, parking areas,
storage areas; any stream, creek, river or body of water; or vacant land and
recreation facilities.
   PUBLIC PROPERTY. Any area that is used or held out for use by the public,
whether owned or operated by public or private interests, including, but not
limited to, highways, streets, alleys, parks, recreation areas, sidewalks,
medians, lakes, rivers, streams, ponds and other bodies of water.
   RUBBISH and TRASH. Waste material not to include food wastes.
   SCHOOL CONTAINER. A container placed and maintained by a school or its
agents for use by the school system.
   SCHOOL SOLID WASTE. Garbage, rubbish and trash resulting from the normal
operation of the school system.
   SEMI-TRAILER. Every vehicle of the trailer type so designed and used in
conjunction with a motor vehicle that some part of its own weight and that of
its own load rests upon or is carried by another vehicle.
   TRAILER. Every vehicle without motive power designed for carrying property
or passengers wholly on its own structure and for being drawn by a motor
vehicle.
   VEHICLE. Every device capable or being moved upon a public highway or public
waterway, and in, upon or by which any person or property may be transported or
drawn upon a public highway or waterway, and shall also include any watercraft,
boat, ship, vessel, barge or other floating craft, except devices moved by
human power or used exclusively upon stationary rails.
(Prior Code, § 14-58) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-59 VIOLATIONS OF ARTICLE.
   (A)   Unless otherwise specifically provided, a violation of any provision
of this article shall constitute a Class 3 misdemeanor.
   (B)   Enforcement officers of the County Sheriff’s Department, the State
Division of Game and Inland Fisheries, and all other police agencies with the
power to arrest are hereby empowered to issue citations to or arrest persons
violating any provision of this article, and may serve and execute all warrants
and other process issued in enforcing the provisions of this article.
   (C)   The Building Official, animal warden and Litter Control Coordinator
may issue citations for violations of this article.
   (D)   Prosecution for a violation of any provision of this article may be
initiated by any law enforcement officer who witnesses such offense or who
discovers an article of litter bearing a person’s name or address, liberally
distributed on the property of another, on any public highway, street or road,
upon a public park or recreation area, or upon any other public property,
except property that is designated as a permitted disposal site. Such
prosecution may be initiated by the Litter Coordinator or any private citizen
who witnesses an offense or discovers evidence.
   (E)   In a prosecution for a violation of this article, articles of litter
bearing a person’s name or address, found liberally distributed on the private
property of another, or on any public property as in subsection (D) above,
shall be presumed to be the property of such person whose name or address
appears thereon, and it shall be presumed that such person placed such article
of litter. Such presumption shall be rebuttable by competent evidence.
   (F)   When an authorized person issues a notice for a violation of this
article, he or she shall serve the offending person by:
      (1)   Delivering a copy of the notice to whom it is directed in person;
      (2)   If the party cannot be found, by delivering a copy and giving
information of its contents and meaning to any member of the family or employee
found at the offending person’s regular place of abode or usual place of
business; or
      (3)   By mailing, by certified mail, a copy of the notice to the last
known address of the person.
   (G)   For violations of this article, the county may take clean-up,
corrective, repair or replacement measures, and the expense thereof shall be an
obligation of the violator and shall be a lien on his or her property, subject
to collection as taxes and levies are collected or by any other appropriate
means.
   (H)   (1)   The governing body of the county shall, through its Litter
Control Officer and County Attorney, be authorized in accordance with VA Code
§§ 15.2-901 and 10.1-1418.1, and any other applicable statutes and ordinances,
including claims for court costs and attorney’s fees.
      (2)   Should any part or provision of this article be found to be invalid
due to conflict with federal or state law or regulations, or found to be
otherwise invalid by any court of competent jurisdiction, such invalidity shall
in no way affect any other provision of this article and the invalid portion of
such ordinance shall be deemed to be deleted herefrom without affecting any
other provision of this article.
(Prior Code, § 14-59) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984; Ord. passed 8-25-1989; Ord. 216-
10, passed 2-16-2010)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for class 3 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§ 14-60 STANDARDS FOR LITTER RECEPTACLES AND TRASH CONTAINERS.
   Standards for the construction, placement, use, service and maintenance of
litter receptacles and trash containers shall be as prescribed by the Board of
Supervisors. Any receptacle or container which does not conform to such
standards shall be replaced by the owner or user of the receptacle or container
upon written notice from the county. Failure to do so within 90 days shall
constitute a violation of this section and each day thereafter shall constitute
a separate violation.
(Prior Code, § 14-60) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-61 FEE FOR USE OF COUNTY LANDFILL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to dispose of trash or garbage on any
county landfill or waste transfer station before paying the fees established
from time to time by the Board of Supervisors. A schedule of such fees shall be
maintained in the office of the County Administrator and shall be open to
inspection during regular business hours.
(Prior Code, § 14-61) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984; Ord. passed 7-18-2000)
§ 14-62 COMMERCIAL WASTE COLLECTORS.
   All persons engaged in the operation of a waste collection service in the
county for a profit shall use vehicles which are constructed or covered in such
a manner as to prevent the distribution of waste. Such persons shall dispose of
waste only on a permitted disposal site.
(Prior Code, § 14-62) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-63 LITTERING GENERALLY.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to drop, deposit, discard or
otherwise dispose of litter in or upon any public or private property within
the county including, but not restricted to, any street, sidewalk, park,
stream, river, vacant or occupied lot, except in containers, bulk waste
containers or receptacles, or in an area designated by the state or county as a
permitted disposal site.
   (B)   When a violation of the provisions of this section has been observed
by any person, and the matter dumped or disposed of has been ejected from a
motor vehicle, the owner or operator of such motor vehicle shall be presumed to
be the person ejecting such matter. Such presumption shall be rebuttable by
competent evidence.
   (C)   A violation of this section shall constitute a Class 1 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-63) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 1 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions and authority of county to adopt above section, see VA
Code Title 33.2, Chapter 8
§ 14-64 INDISCRIMINATE DUMPING OR DISCARDING OF LITTER AND SOLID WASTE.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to discard or dump any item or
combination of items of any type of waste defined in §
14-58, with a singular or combined volume of 12 cubic inches or more, or any
animal carcass, along any street or road, on or off the right-of-way, or on any
public or private property, stream, river or body of water, except in an area
designated for such use by the county or the state.
(Prior Code, § 14-64) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-65 LITTERING WITH HANDBILLS AND OTHER ADVERTISING MATERIAL.
   It shall be unlawful for any person distributing commercial handbills,
leaflets, flyers or any other advertising and information material to
distribute material in such a manner that it litters either public or private
property through the action or reasonably foreseeable action of wind or
animals.
(Prior Code, § 14-65) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-66 ESCAPE OF VEHICLE LOADS.
   (A)   No vehicle used to transport litter or other items likely to fall or
be blown from such vehicle shall be driven or moved, stopped, or parked on any
highway, unless such vehicle is covered to prevent any of its load from
dropping, sifting, leaking or otherwise escaping therefrom; provided, however,
that sand or any substance to increase traction, or water or other substance,
may be applied on a roadway in the cleaning or maintaining of such roadway by
the state or local government agency having such responsibilities.
   (B)   Any person operating a vehicle from which any glass or objects have
fallen, escaped or been ejected which would cause an obstruction or damage a
vehicle, or otherwise endanger travelers or animals on public property, shall
immediately cause the public property to be cleaned of all glass or objects and
shall pay any costs therefor.
   (C)   A violation of this section shall constitute a Class 1 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-66) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 1 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see VA Code § 10.1-1424
§ 14-67 AREAS SURROUNDING COMMERCIAL ESTABLISHMENTS AND INSTITUTIONS TO BE
LITTER FREE.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of each proprietor, owner and operator of any
business, industry or institution to keep the adjacent and surrounding area
clean and free of litter.
   (B)   These areas include, but are not limited to, public and private
sidewalks; roads and alleys; grounds; parking lots; loading and unloading
areas; and all vacant lots which are owned or leased by such establishment or
institution.
(Prior Code, § 14-67) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-68 EXTERIOR OF RESIDENTIAL PROPERTY TO BE LITTER FREE.
   It shall be the duty of each residential property owner and tenant to keep
all exterior private property free of litter. These areas shall include, but
not be restricted to, sidewalks, alleys and driveways; yards and grounds;
fences, walls and property lines; drainages; and vacant lots in residential
area.
(Prior Code, § 14-68) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-69 LITTER AT CONSTRUCTION AND DEMOLITION SITES.
   It shall be unlawful for any owner, agent or contractor to permit the
accumulation of litter at the site of any construction or demolition project.
It shall be the duty of the owner, agent or contractor in charge to collect and
contain all litter on a regular basis. All litter shall be removed from such
site as necessary to prevent health and safety hazards.
(Prior Code, § 14-69) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-70 SWEEPING LITTER INTO STREET.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to sweep or push litter from sidewalks
into streets. Such litter shall be deposited in a proper receptacle or
container.
(Prior Code, § 14-70) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-71 HOUSEHOLD SOLID WASTE CONTAINERIZATION AND REMOVAL.
   (A)   All household solid waste shall be containerized in such a manner as
to prevent or preclude distribution by wind or by animal.
   (B)   Such waste shall be placed for collection into a county collection
container (dumpster), taken directly to a permitted disposal site during
working hours, placed for collection by a commercial waste hauler or otherwise
legally disposed of.
(Prior Code, § 14-71) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-72 COMMERCIAL AND INSTITUTION SOLID WASTE CONTAINERIZATION AND REMOVAL.
   All commercial and institution solid waste shall be containerized in such a
manner to prevent or preclude distribution by wind or animal. Such waste shall
be placed for collection into a private collection container (dumpster), taken
directly to a permitted disposal site during working hours, placed for
collection by a commercial waste hauler or otherwise legally disposed of.
(Prior Code, § 14-72) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-73 SCHOOL SOLID WASTE CONTAINERIZATION AND REMOVAL.
   All school solid waste shall be containerized in such a manner as to prevent
or preclude distribution by wind or animal. Such waste shall be placed for
collection into a school collection container (dumpster), taken directly to a
permitted disposal site during working hours, placed for collection by a
commercial waste hauler or otherwise legally disposed of.
(Prior Code, § 14-73) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-74 IMPROPER DISPOSAL OF BULK WASTE AND BRUSH.
   (A)   Bulk waste shall not be deposited into any container or receptacle, or
indiscriminately dumped.
   (B)   Brush shall not be deposited into any container, bulk waste container
or receptacle, or indiscriminately dumped.
(Prior Code, § 14-74) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-75 DISPOSAL OF WASTE BY NON-RESIDENTS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person residing outside the county to dispose
of any bulk waste or household, commercial, institution or county governmental
solid waste, either properly or improperly, within the county, without the
express consent of the Board of Supervisors or the County Administrator;
provided, however, that tourists, visitors and other transients may dispose of
household waste if done in accordance with this article.
(Prior Code, § 14-75) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-76 DAMAGING OR DEFACING RECEPTACLES OR CONTAINERS GENERALLY.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to damage or deface, or cause the same
to be done to, any receptacle, container or bulk waste container.
(Prior Code, § 14-76)
§ 14-77 SETTING AFIRE RECEPTACLE OR CONTAINER.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to set afire or cause to be set afire
any container, bulk waste container or receptacle. A violation of this section
shall constitute a Class 1 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-77) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 1 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§ 14-78 DISPLACING RECEPTACLES OR CONTAINERS.
   It shall be unlawful for any person not authorized to do so, to displace or
cause to be displaced any receptacle, container or bulk waste container.
(Prior Code, § 14-78) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-79 DEPOSIT OF ANIMAL CARCASS IN RECEPTACLE OR CONTAINER.
   No person shall deposit any animal carcass in a receptacle, container or
bulk waste container.
(Prior Code, § 14-79) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-80 PROHIBITED DEPOSITS IN SCHOOL CONTAINER.
   No person shall dispose of any type of waste into a school container, except
that which is generated by the school system.
(Prior Code, § 14-80) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-81 UNAUTHORIZED USE OF RECEPTACLES OR CONTAINERS BY BUSINESS OR
INSTITUTION.
   No business or institution shall use any county container, bulk waste
container or receptacle; provided for use by the public for the deposit of any
type of waste generated by the business or institution.
(Prior Code, § 14-81) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-82 CARDBOARD BOXES TO BE FLATTENED PRIOR TO PLACEMENT IN CONTAINER.
   Large cardboard boxes, large quantities of small cardboard boxes and similar
items requiring large volumes of space for disposal shall not be deposited in
any container without first being flattened.
(Prior Code, § 14-82) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-83 SCAVENGING FROM OR IMPEDING SERVICING OF RECEPTACLES OR CONTAINERS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to go through the contents or
remove any item from a container, bulk waste container or receptacle, unless
authorized to do so.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to impede or cause to be impeded
the servicing of any container, bulk waste container or receptacle.
(Prior Code, § 14-83) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
§ 14-84 DEPOSIT OF DANGEROUS MATERIAL AT WASTE COLLECTION OR DISPOSAL
LOCATIONS.
   (A)   No person shall place, deposit or dump any explosive, gasoline,
gasoline derivative, or other inflammable or noxious, poisonous, burning or
other dangerous material in or at county solid waste collection or disposal
locations.
   (B)   A violation of this section shall constitute a Class 1 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 14-84) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 1 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§ 14-85 OPEN STORAGE OF INOPERABLE VEHICLES OR MOTOR VEHICLE PARTS.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, except within a fully
enclosed building or structure, or otherwise shielded or screened from view, on
any public or private property, any motor vehicle, trailer or semi-trailer
which is inoperative. As used in this section, an INOPERATIVE MOTOR VEHICLE is
any motor vehicle which is not in operating condition or which, for a period of
60 days or longer, has been partially or totally disassembled by the removal of
tires and wheels, the engine or other essential parts required for operation of
the vehicle, or on which there are displayed neither valid license plates nor a
valid inspection decal. The provisions of this section shall not apply to a
licensed business, which on September 7, 1984, was regularly engaged in
business as an automobile dealer, salvage dealer or scrap processor.
   (B)   The accumulation and storage of parts of motor vehicles on private or
public property or rights-of-way shall be unlawful, except within a fully
enclosed building or structure, or unless such parts are otherwise shielded or
screened from view.
   (C)   If any person empowered to issue citations under this article finds
any violation of this section, such person shall make diligent search and
inquiry to determine the record owner of the land upon which the vehicle or
parts are located or the owner of the vehicle or parts, and shall notify the
owner as directed by §
14-59 that such violation has been found and the nature thereof. The notice
shall demand and it shall be the duty of the record owner of the land or
vehicle or parts to cause such vehicle or parts to be removed from the property
forthwith and taken to an authorized place of storage or disposal. Such removal
shall be accomplished within 30 days of the date of mailing or service of the
notice.
   (D)   If the mailing address of the owner of the land and the owner of the
vehicle or parts found in violation of this section is not known and diligent
search has been made to determine same and the land is unoccupied and the owner
has no agent in the county, provided for in this section, shall be posted upon
such land as notice to the owner thereof.
   (E)   If the violation described in the notice has not been remedied within
30 days after the mailing, serving or posting thereof, the owner of the land on
which the vehicle or parts are located or the owner of the vehicle or parts, or
both of them, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor for maintaining a public
nuisance. In addition, the county shall have an injunctive action for any
continuing or anticipated violation of this section. Each day that the
offending vehicle or parts are allowed to remain on the property in violation
of this section after the passage of 30 days shall constitute a separate
violation.
   (F)   The provisions of this section shall not apply to an antique motor
vehicle that is capable of being repaired or restored, and the parts necessary
for such repairing or restoration; provided:
      (1)   A bona fide effort is being made to repair or restore such vehicle;
and
      (2)   Such vehicle and parts are covered so as to shield them from public
view, protect them from the weather and make them unsuitable as a hiding place
for snakes, rats or vermin. Such shield shall be constructed of wood, metal,
masonry or vegetative material of such density as to screen the vehicle and
parts from public view, and shall be constructed and thereafter maintained in
such a manner as not to create or perpetuate neighborhood blight.
(Prior Code, § 14-85) (Ord. passed 9-7-1984)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code Title 15.2, Chapter 11
