ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
§ 15-1 DUE DATE FOR RETURNS ON TANGIBLE PERSONAL PROPERTY.
   Tangible personal property returns shall be due on May 1 of each year.
(Prior Code, § 15-1) (Ord. passed 10-8-1980)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code § 58.1-3916
§ 15-2 DUE DATE FOR TAXES ON REAL ESTATE AND TANGIBLE PERSONAL PROPERTY.
   Taxes or levies on real estate and tangible personal property shall be due
and payable on October 31 of each year.
(Prior Code, § 15-2) (Ord. passed 10-8-1980; Ord. passed 12-17-2019)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code § 58.1-3916
§ 15-3 INTEREST AND PENALTY ON DELINQUENT REAL ESTATE AND TANGIBLE PERSONAL
PROPERTY TAXES.
   (A)   Interest, calculated at the rate of 10% per annum, shall be charged on
delinquent payments of real estate and tangible personal property taxes. Such
interest shall commence on November 1, the first day of the month next
following the month in which such taxes are due.
   (B)   The penalty for failure to pay a tangible personal property or real
estate tax when due shall be 10% of the amount past due or the sum of $2,
whichever is greater. Such penalty shall be assessed on November 1, the first
day of the month next following the month in which such taxes are due.
(Prior Code, § 15-3) (Ord. passed 10-8-1980; Ord. passed 1-10-1986; Ord. passed
12-17-2019)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code § 58.1-3916
§ 15-4 CERTAIN PERSONAL PROPERTY EXEMPT FROM TAXATION.
   Pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3505, the following classes of personal property
shall be exempt from taxation by the county: horses, mules and other kindred
animals; cattle; sheep and goats; hogs; poultry; and farm machinery and farm
implements of every kind and description.
(Prior Code, § 15-4) (Ord. passed 8-3-1983)
§ 15-5 PURPOSE; DEFINITIONS; RELATION TO OTHER ORDINANCES.
   (A)   The purpose of §§
15-5 through
15-5.3 is to provide for the implementation of the changes to the Personal
Property Tax Relief Act, being VA Code Title 58.1, Chapter 35.1.
   (B)   Terms used in §§
15-5 through
15-5.3 that have defined meanings set forth in Personal Property Tax Relief Act
shall have the same meanings as set forth in VA Code § 58.1-3523, as amended.
   (C)   To the extent that the provisions of §§
15-5 through
15-5.3 conflict with any prior ordinance or provision of the county, §§
15-5 through
15-5.3 shall control.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2005)
§ 15-5.1 METHOD OF COMPUTING AND REFLECTING TAX RELIEF.
   (A)   For tax years commencing in 2006, the county adopts the provisions of
Item 503.E of the 2005 Appropriations Act; providing for the computation of tax
relief as a specific dollar amount to be off-set against the total taxes that
would otherwise be due, but for personal property tax relief and the reporting
of such specific dollar relief on the tax bill.
   (B)   The Board shall, by resolution, set the percentage of tax relief at
such a level that it is anticipated fully to exhaust Personal Property Tax
Relief Act, being VA Code Title 58.1, Chapter 35.1, relief funds provided to
the county by the commonwealth.
   (C)   Personal property tax bills shall set forth on their face the specific
dollar amount of relief credited with respect to each qualifying vehicle,
together with an explanation of the general manner in which relief is
allocated.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2005)
§ 15-5.2 ALLOCATION OF RELIEF AMONG TAXPAYERS.
   (A)   Allocation of personal property tax relief shall be provided in
accordance with the general provisions of this section, as implemented by the
specific provisions of the county annual budget relating to Personal Property
Tax Relief Act relief.
   (B)   Relief with respect to qualifying vehicles with assessed values of
more than $100 shall be provided at a percentage, annually fixed and applied to
the first $20,000 in value of each such qualifying vehicle that is estimated
fully to use all available state personal property tax relief funding. The
percentage shall be established annually.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2005)
§ 15-5.3 TRANSITIONAL PROVISIONS.
   (A)   Pursuant to authority conferred in Item 503.D of the 2005
Appropriations Act, unless the assessment is determined to be of no fault of
the taxpayer, the County Treasurer is authorized to issue a supplemental
personal property tax bill, in the amount of 100% of tax due without regard to
any former entitlement to state personal property tax relief, plus applicable
penalties and interest, to any taxpayer whose taxes with respect to a
qualifying vehicle for tax year 2005 or any prior tax year remain unpaid on
September 1, 2006, or such date as state funds for reimbursement of the state
share of such bill have become unavailable, whichever earlier occurs.
   (B)   Penalty and interest with respect to bills issued pursuant to
subsection (A) above shall be computed on the entire amount of tax owed.
Interest shall be computed at the rate provided in §
15-3 from the original due date of the tax.
(Ord. passed 12-20-2005)
§ 15-6 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of §§
15-6 through
15-9, the following definitions shall apply unless the context clearly
indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ELIGIBLE VEHICLE. Titled in the qualified taxpayer’s name, either jointly or
solely, and proof of such ownership and a copy of current registration must be
provided to the Commissioner along with application for exemption; it must be
for personal use only, located, taxed and tagged in the county. Commercial
vehicles are not eligible for any exemption under §§
15-6 through
15-9 .
   QUALIFIED TAXPAYER. A taxpayer who:
      (1)   Is an active member of a volunteer fire department or a volunteer
rescue squad located in and operating in the county, as verified by the
department chief or squad captain, and has been active for a minimum of two
years prior to application, without receiving any compensation for such
volunteer duties;
      (2)   Is not delinquent on any real or personal property taxes previously
assessed by the county;
      (3)   Is included on his or her department’s roster, in the case of a
firefighter, which is filed with the County Circuit Court Clerk’s office;
      (4)   Is certified as qualified by the County Emergency Management
Coordinator;
      (5)   The chief of each volunteer fire department shall on or before
January 15 of each year submit to the Emergency Management Coordinator a
certification form, which contains information to verify eligibility of the
department’s members, together with a copy of the roster certification stamped
filed with the County Circuit Court Clerk. The certification form shall be as
attached hereto;
      (6)   Is a resident of the county and lists the county as their domicile;
and
      (7)   Accumulates a total of 30 points annually, on a calendar year
basis, with points earned as follows:
 
Classes and/or course trainings
   4 hours or less           1 point each
   Over 4 hours              2 points each
Department or squad meeting     1 point each (max of 12)
attendance
Response calls                  2 points each
Training sessions               1 point each
*   Records subject to audit by the Commissioner of the Revenue to verify
the minimum point threshold is met
 
(Ord. passed 3-19-2019)
§ 15-7 EXEMPTION.
   (A)   All or a portion of the value of a single automobile owned or leased
by a qualified taxpayer, which is subject to local taxation pursuant to VA Code
§§ 58.1-3500 et seq., shall be exempted from personal property taxation as
hereinafter set forth.
   (B)   The aggregate amount of exemptible value pursuant to §§
15-6 through
15-9 shall be determined annually by the Board of Supervisors in their annual
budget on or before June 30 each year. No exemption shall exceed $200 per
qualified taxpayer on their personal property obligation, in any given year.
Upon approval of Board’s annual budget on or before June 30 each year, the
County Administrator or its designee shall advise the Commissioner in writing
of the amount budgeted by the Board for the purposes of §§
15-6 through
15-9. The exemptible value per qualified taxpayer, who applies for and is
granted the exemption, shall be the aggregate amount of exemptible value set by
the Board of Supervisors divided by the total number of qualified taxpayers who
apply for and are granted the exemption.
(Ord. passed 3-19-2019)
§ 15-8 PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Each year on or before March 31, the Emergency Management Coordinator
shall submit to the Commissioner of the Revenue a list of eligible qualified
taxpayers.
   (B)   Any qualified taxpayer may submit to the Commissioner of the Revenue
an application, in a form approved by the Commissioner, on or before March 31
of each year to receive the exemption. However, the Commissioner of the Revenue
shall be authorized, in his or her discretion, and for good cause shown and
without fault on the part of the qualified taxpayer, to accept a certification
after the March 31 deadline.
   (C)   The Commissioner shall, using the list submitted by the Emergency
Management Coordinator, determine which applicants are eligible for the
exemption.
   (D)   The Commissioner then shall exempt a portion of the value each
eligible applicant’s eligible vehicle, according to the formula herein set
forth, from taxation for that tax year. Should the exemptible value available
for any qualified taxpayer exceed the value of such taxpayer’s eligible
vehicle, the entire value of such vehicle shall be exempted; no remaining
exemptible value shall be allocated to the taxpayer.
(Ord. passed 3-19-2019)
§ 15-9 APPEALS.
   (A)   Any applicant who believes he or she was eligible for the exemption
but was not listed by the Emergency Management Coordinator as qualified, may
appeal to the Board of Supervisors by giving written notice to the County
Administrator within 30 days of receiving his or her tax assessment.
   (B)   Any applicant who was designated by the Emergency Management
Coordinator as eligible for the exemption but was not granted the exemption by
the Commissioner, may be appeal said decision as provided in the Code of
Virginia for assessments generally.
(Ord. passed 3-19-2019)
§ 15-10 SPECIAL PROVISIONS FOR CERTAIN EQUIPMENT AND ENABLING SOFTWARE USED IN
A DATA CENTER.
   (A)   There is hereby levied a tax of $0.24 on each $100 of assessed value
of computer equipment or enabling software used in a data center meeting the
requirements of VA Code § 58.1-609.3(18). This levy shall be in lieu of any
other personal property tax on such property.
   (B)   All other assessments, taxes and fees imposed by the county shall
remain in full force and effect.
(Ord. 21-00, passed 7-20-2021)
§ 15-11 REFUND OF EXCESS PROCEEDS FROM SALE OF REAL PROPERTY FOR DELINQUENT
TAXES.
   There is authorized the refund of excess proceeds from the sale of real
property for delinquent taxes, under the condition stated previously, is hereby
approved and shall be effective on a case by case basis by the adoption of a
resolution stating the amount of relief to be granted in the form of a refund
to said former owner, heir, or assign, or unknown beneficiary.
(Ord. passed 2-18-2020)
§ 15-12 PAYMENT OF ADMINISTRATIVE COSTS BY DELINQUENT TAXPAYERS.
   (A)   Delinquent taxpayers shall pay a fee to cover the administrative costs
and reasonable attorney’s or collection agency’s fees actually contracted for,
not to exceed 20% of the taxes or other charges so collected. Such
administrative costs shall be in addition to all penalties and interest, and
shall not exceed $20 for taxes collected subsequent to the filing of a warrant
or other appropriate legal document but prior to judgment, and $25 for taxes
collected subsequent to judgment.
   (B)   No tax assessment or tax bill shall be deemed delinquent and subject
to collection procedures prescribed herein during the pendency of any
administrative appeal under VA Code § 58.1-3980, 1950, as amended, so long as
the appeal is filed within 90 days of appeal; provided that nothing in this
subsection (B) shall be construed to preclude the assessment or refund,
following the final determination of such appeal, of such interest as otherwise
may be provided by general law as to the portion of a tax bill which has
remained unpaid or was overpaid during the pendency of such appeal and is
determined in such appeal to be properly due and owing.
(Ord. passed 4-30-1998)
§§ 15-13—5-14 RESERVED.
ARTICLE II. REAL ESTATE TAX EXEMPTION FOR ELDERLY AND DISABLED PERSONS
§ 15-15 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   AFFIDAVIT. The real estate tax exemption affidavit (a sworn statement in
writing).
   DWELLING. The full-time residence of the person claiming an exemption.
   EXEMPTION. Exemption from the county real estate tax according to the
provisions of this article.
   PERMANENTLY AND TOTALLY DISABLED. A person that is unable to engage in any
substantial gainful activity by reason of any medically determinable physical
or mental impairment or deformity which can be expected to result in death or
can be expected to last for the duration of such person’s life.
   PROPERTY. Real property.
   TAXABLE YEAR. The calendar year, from January 1 until December 31, for which
an exemption is claimed.
(Prior Code, § 15-15) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Cross-reference:
   Definitions and rules of construction generally, see §
1-2
Statutory reference:
   Similar definition of permanently and totally disabled, see VA Code § 58.1-
3217
§ 15-16 EXEMPTION AUTHORIZED.
   (A)   Real estate tax exemption is provided for qualified property owners
who are 65 years of age or older or permanently and totally disabled, and who
are eligible according to the terms of this article.
   (B)   Persons qualifying for exemption are deemed to be bearing an
extraordinary real estate tax burden in relation to their income and financial
worth.
(Prior Code, § 15-16) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
§ 15-17 ADMINISTRATION OF EXEMPTION.
   The exemption shall be administered by the Commissioner of the Revenue
according to the provisions of this article. The Commissioner is hereby
authorized and empowered to prescribe, adopt, promulgate and enforce rules and
regulations in conformance with the provisions of this article, including the
requirement of answers under oath, as may be reasonably necessary to determine
qualifications for exemption as specified by this article. The Commissioner may
require the production of certified tax returns and appraisal reports to
establish income or financial worth.
(Prior Code, § 15-17) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority to make inquiries and require answers under oath and production of
tax returns, see VA Code § 58.1-3213(F)
§ 15-18 QUALIFICATIONS FOR EXEMPTION.
   Exemption shall be granted to persons subject to the following provisions:
   (A)   The title of the property for which exemption is claimed is held, or
partially held, on January 1 of the taxable year, by the person claiming
exemption;
   (B)   The head of the household occupying the dwelling and owning title, or
partial title, thereto is determined to be 65 years old or older or permanently
and totally disabled on December 31 of the year immediately preceding the
taxable year;
   (C)   The gross combined income of the owner during the year immediately
preceding the taxable year shall not exceed $25,000. Gross combined income
shall include income from all sources of the owner and of the owner’s relatives
living in the dwelling for which exemption is claimed, excluding the first
$2,000 of the relative’s income. Any form of public welfare assistance (other
than medical care for the medically indigent) must be listed as income; and
   (D)   The total combined financial worth of the owner, as of December 31 of
the year immediately preceding the taxable year, shall not exceed $85,000.
Total financial worth shall include the value of all assets, including
equitable interests, of the owner and the owner’s relatives living in the
dwelling for which exemption is claimed, and shall exclude the fair market
value of the dwelling and the land upon which it is situated, not exceeding one
acre, for which exemption is claimed.
(Prior Code, § 15-18) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority of county as to income and financial worth requirements, see VA
Code § 58.1-3212
§ 15-19 CLAIMANT’S AFFIDAVIT AND CERTIFICATION OF DISABILITY.
   (A)   Annually, and not later than May 1 of the taxable year, the person
claiming an exemption must file a real estate tax exemption affidavit with the
Commissioner of the Revenue. The affidavit shall set forth, in a manner
prescribed by the Commissioner of the Revenue, the names of all persons
occupying the dwelling for which exemption is claimed, their gross combined
income and their total combined net worth.
   (B)   If the person claiming exemption is under 65 years of age, the
affidavit shall have attached thereto a certification by the Social Security
Administration, the Department of Veterans Affairs or the Railroad Retirement
Board, or if such person is not eligible for certification by any of these
agencies, a sworn affidavit by two medical doctors who are either licensed to
practice medicine in the commonwealth or are military officers on active duty
who practice medicine with the United States Armed Forces, to the effect that
such person is permanently and totally disabled, as defined in §
15-15 and in VA Code § 58.1-3217; however, a certification pursuant to 42
U.S.C. § 423(d) by the Social Security Administration, so long as the person
remains eligible for such social security benefits shall be deemed to satisfy
such definition. The affidavit of at least one of the doctors shall be based
upon a physical examination of the person by such doctor. The affidavit of one
of the doctors may be based upon medical information contained in the records
of the Civil Service Commission which is relevant to the standards for
determining permanent and total disability.
(Prior Code, § 15-19) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Authority of county to fix date for filing affidavit, see VA Code § 58.1-
3213(E)
   Similar provisions, see VA Code § 58.1-3213(A), (D)
§ 15-20 CERTIFICATION TO COUNTY TREASURER; DEDUCTION FROM TAX LIABILITY.
   If, after audit and investigation, the Commissioner of the Revenue
determines that the claimant is qualified for exemption, the Commissioner shall
so certify to the County Treasurer who shall deduct the amount of the exemption
from the claimant’s real estate tax liability.
(Prior Code, § 15-20) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
§ 15-21 AMOUNT OF EXEMPTION.
   (A)   For qualified persons, the amount of exemption of the real estate tax
shall be determined by the following table:
 
Annual Income     Percent of Tax to be Exempted
$0 - $17,000      100
$17,001 - $19,500 75
$19,501 - $22,000 50
$22,001 - $25,000 25
 
   (B)   After determining which income range the person’s annual income falls
in, the amount of tax exemption will be computed by multiplying the existing
tax bill times the percentage opposite the appropriate income figure, the
result of which will be the amount of tax to be excused. The difference between
the original tax and the figure arrived at will be due the county as the
assessed property tax for that year. In no case will the tax excused exceed
$200.
(Prior Code, § 15-21) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Amount of exemption to be as prescribed by ordinance, see VA Code § 58.1-
3210
§ 15-22 WHEN EXEMPTION EFFECTIVE; REDUCTION APPLIES ONLY IF TAXES PAID WHEN
DUE.
   (A)   The exemption shall be effective only in the current tax year and
shall be applied to reduce taxes, if the taxes due and owing are paid on or
before the due date set by law for payment without penalty. In the event the
taxpayer qualified for exemption owes delinquent real property taxes, the
exemption will be allowed for the current tax year only and all payments
received by the current tax year due date may be credited first to the current
year tax amount.
   (B)   Any payment in excess of the current year amount, less any allowed
exemption, will be applied to the most delinquent tax due, less any accrued
penalty and interest.
(Prior Code, § 15-22) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
§ 15-23 EFFECT OF CHANGES IN STATUS.
   Changes in respect to income, financial worth, ownership of property or
other factors occurring during the tax year for which the affidavit is filed
and having the effect of exceeding or violating the limitations and conditions;
provided in this article shall nullify any relief of real estate tax liability
for the then current taxable year and the taxable year immediately following.
(Prior Code, § 15-23) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see VA Code § 58.1-3215
§ 15-24 FALSE CLAIMS.
   Any person falsely claiming an exemption shall be guilty of a Class 3
misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 15-24) (Ord. passed 3-20-2012)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 3 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§§ 15-25—15-34 RESERVED.
ARTICLE III. BUILDING CONTRACTORS LICENSE TAX
§ 15-35 CONTRACTOR DEFINED.
   CONTRACTOR includes individuals, firms, partnerships, associations,
corporations and combinations of individuals of whatever form or character,
carrying on or continuing a business, profession, trade or occupation incident
to construction of any improvement or structure requiring a building permit by
the county.
(Ord. passed 11-15-1996)
§ 15-36 RATE.
   (A)   There is hereby levied, assessed or imposed a local contractor’s
license tax on a per project basis upon contractors engaged in construction
projects exceeding $100,000 within the county, but outside the boundary of any
town having a similar license tax, which tax shall be in the amount of $30 or
$0.16 per $100 of gross receipts of the contractor as derived from such
construction project performed in the county, whichever amount is greater.
   (B)   The tax shall be collected at such time as the contractor applies for
and receives the building permit through the County Building Inspector’s
office.
   (C)   In the event such building permit is acquired in the name of the
property owner rather than the contractor, the tax shall nonetheless be due and
owing by the property owner at the same rate as if assessed to the contractor.
   (D)   No building permit shall be issued by the county for construction of
any structure or improvement until such time as the contractor’s tax as herein
imposed has been fully paid.
(Ord. passed 11-15-1996)
§ 15-37 INCORPORATION BY REFERENCE.
   The provisions of VA Code § 58.1-3703, as amended, are hereby incorporated
by express reference to be considered a part of this article.
(Ord. passed 11-15-1996)
§ 15-38 PENALTIES.
   (A)   Any person who engages in the contracting business within the county
without first having obtained a license, building permit and having paid the
tax herein imposed, shall pay a penalty of 5% of any amount due hereunder, in
addition to the regular amount, and shall pay interest at the rate of 8% per
annum on any unpaid amount.
   (B)   Any person who violates the provisions of this article by providing
false information as to gross receipts shall be guilty of a Class 1
misdemeanor. Each day of a violation shall constitute a separate and distinct
offense.
(Ord. passed 11-15-1996)
§§ 15-39—15-48 RESERVED.
ARTICLE IV. RETAIL SALES TAX
§ 15-49 LEVIED; TO BE ADDED TO RATE OF STATE SALES TAX AND THE LIKE.
   Pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-605, a local general retail sales tax, at the
rate of 1%, to provide revenue for the general fund of the county, is hereby
levied. Such tax shall be added to the rate of the state sales tax imposed by
VA Code §§ 58.1-603 and 58.1-604 and shall be subject to all provisions of VA
Code Title 58.1, Chapter 6 (§§ 58.1-600 et seq.), all the amendments thereto
and the rules and regulations published with respect thereto.
(Prior Code, § 15-49) (Ord. passed 5-4-1966)
§ 15-50 PRICE BRACKETS; NO DISCOUNT.
   For the sales tax levied by this article, the applicable brackets of prices
shall be as prescribed in VA Code § 58.1-628 for the combined state and local
tax. No discount under VA Code § 58.1-622 shall be allowed on the tax levied by
this article.
(Prior Code, § 15-50)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see VA Code § 58.1-605
§ 15-51 ADMINISTRATION AND COLLECTION.
   Pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-605, the local general retail sales tax levied
pursuant to this article shall be administered and collected by the State Tax
Commissioner in the same manner and subject to the same penalties as provided
for the state sales tax, with the adjustments required by VA Code § 58.1-628.
(Prior Code, § 15-51) (Ord. passed 5-4-1966)
§ 15-52 EXEMPTIONS.
   All fuels for domestic consumption shall be exempt from the sales tax levied
by this article.
(Prior Code, § 15-52) (Ord. passed 11-15-1981)
Statutory reference:
   Authority for exemption, see VA Code § 58.1-609
§§ 15-53—15-62 RESERVED.
ARTICLE V. TAX ON PURCHASERS OF UTILITY SERVICES
§ 15-63 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   PURCHASER. Any person who purchases a utility service.
   SELLER. Any person, organization, firm, corporation, cooperative, sanitary
district, municipality or any other entity who or which sells or provides a
utility service.
   UTILITY SERVICE. Local exchange telephone service and electric service
furnished within the county.
(Prior Code, § 15-63) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
Cross-reference:
   Definitions and rules of construction generally, see §
1-2
§ 15-64 IMPOSED; EXCEPTIONS GENERALLY.
   (A)   There is hereby imposed and levied by the county upon each and every
purchaser of a utility service a tax for general purposes in the amount of 15%
of the charge, exclusive of any federal or state tax thereon, made by the
seller against the purchaser with respect to such service; provided, however,
that in case a monthly bill submitted by the seller for the service exceeds
$15, there shall be no tax computed on so much of such bill as exceeds $15.
There shall be no tax computed on bills submitted for electric service for
water heating where a separate meter is used solely for water heating service
or on bills submitted for unmetered electric service.
   (B)   For the purposes of this section, bills shall be considered monthly
bills if submitted 12 times annually for a period of approximately one month or
portion thereof. In case bills are submitted by any seller for two month’s
service, there shall be no tax computed on so much of such bill as exceeds $30.
In the event bills are rendered for utility services stated on a basis other
than one month or two months, the tax imposed by this section shall be computed
pro rata as if such bill was rendered on a monthly basis with the rates and the
maximums set out in this section applied.
(Prior Code, § 15-64) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985; Ord. passed 6-29-1989)
Statutory reference:
   Authority for above tax, see VA Code§ 58.1-3814
§ 15-65 APPLICATION TO TELEPHONE SERVICE.
   The tax imposed and levied by this article on purchasers with respect to
telephone service shall apply to all charges made for local exchange service
except as follows.
   (A)   The total amount of the guaranteed charge on each bill rendered for
semi-public coin box telephone service shall be included in the basis for the
tax with respect to the purchaser of such service, but no other tax shall be
imposed on telephone service paid for by inserting coins in coin-operated
telephones.
   (B)   With respect to flat rate and flat message rate service, the tax shall
apply to only the amount payable for local area service and shall not apply to
any specific charge for calls to points outside the county or to any general
charge or rate differential payable for the privilege of calling points outside
the county.
   (C)   Where purchasers of telephone service are charged on a message rate
basis, the tax shall apply only to the basic charge for such service and shall
not apply to any charge for additional message units.
(Prior Code, § 15-65) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-66 EXEMPTIONS.
   The United States of America, diplomatic personnel exempted by the laws of
the United States, the state and the political subdivisions, boards,
commissions, authorities and agencies thereof, churches, and residences of
ministers of churches owned by a religious body are exempt from the payment of
the tax imposed and levied by this article, with respect to the purchase of
utility services used by such entities.
(Prior Code, § 15-66) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-67 COMPUTATION WHEN SELLER COLLECTS CHARGES IN STATED PERIODS.
   In all cases where the seller collects the charge for a utility service in
stated periods, the tax imposed and levied by this article shall be computed on
the amount of purchases during the month or period according to each bill
rendered; provided that the amount of tax to be collected shall be the nearest
whole cent to the amount computed.
(Prior Code, § 15-67) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-68 DUTY OF PURCHASER TO PAY.
   Each purchaser of a utility service shall pay the tax imposed and levied by
this article at the time the purchase price is paid to the seller of the
utility service. In the event a purchaser makes a partial payment, the tax must
be paid at the time the final portion of the purchase price is paid.
(Prior Code, § 15-68) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-69 DUTY OF SELLER TO COLLECT, REPORT AND REMIT.
   (A)   It shall be the duty of every seller, in acting as the tax collection
medium or agency for the county, to collect from the purchaser, for use of the
county, the tax imposed and levied by this article at the time of collecting
the purchase price charged for the utility service. Taxes so collected during
each calendar month or billing period shall be reported and paid by the seller
to the County Treasurer by the last day of the second calendar month
thereafter, together with the name and address of any purchaser who has paid
his or her total purchase price but has failed to pay the tax imposed by this
article.
   (B)   The County Treasurer may prescribe forms for the filing of any report
or the payment of any funds under this section.
   (C)   The County Treasurer may extend, for good cause shown, the time of
filing the report and payment of the tax by the seller, as required by this
section; provided, however, that no such extension shall exceed a period of 90
days.
(Prior Code, § 15-69) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-70 SELLER’S RECORDS.
   Each seller shall keep complete records showing all purchasers of utility
services in the county, which records shall show the price charged against each
purchaser with respect to each purchase, the date thereof and the date of
payment thereof, and the amount of tax imposed under this article. Such records
shall be kept open for inspection by the duly authorized agents of the county,
who shall have the right, power and authority to make such transcripts thereof
during such times as they may desire.
(Prior Code, § 15-70) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-71 DUTY OF TREASURER TO COLLECT FROM SELLER.
   The County Treasurer is charged with the duty of collecting the taxes
imposed and levied under this article from the seller of the utility service.
(Prior Code, § 15-71) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
§ 15-72 FAILURE OF PURCHASER TO PAY; VIOLATION OF ARTICLE BY SELLER.
   (A)   Any purchaser who fails to pay the tax imposed or levied by this
article and any seller violating the provisions of this article, and any
officer, agent or employee of any seller violating the provisions of this
article shall be guilty of a Class 3 misdemeanor.
   (B)   Upon failing to pay the tax imposed by this article when the total
purchase price is paid, or when the final portion of a purchase price paid in
partial payments is paid, each day’s continuance of failing to pay shall
constitute a separate offense.
   (C)   A conviction for a violation of this article shall not relieve any
person from the payment, collection and remittance of the tax as provided in
this article.
(Prior Code, § 15-72) (Ord. passed 4-1-1985)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 3 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§§ 15-73—15-82 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VI. BANK FRANCHISE TAX
§ 15-83 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BANK. As defined in VA Code § 58.1-1201.
   NET CAPITAL. A bank’s new capital computed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-1205.
(Prior Code, § 15-83) (Ord. passed 6-4-1980)
§ 15-84 IMPOSED.
   There is hereby imposed upon each bank located outside any incorporated
town, but otherwise within the boundaries of this county, a tax on net capital
equalling 80% of the state rate of franchise tax set forth in VA Code § 58.1-
1204. If such bank also has offices that are located outside the county or
within the corporate limits of a town in the county, the tax shall be
apportioned as provided in VA Code § 58.1-1211.
(Prior Code, § 15-84) (Ord. passed 6-4-1980)
Statutory reference:
   Authority for above tax, see VA Code § 58.1-210
§ 15-85 FILING OF RETURNS, SCHEDULES AND THE LIKE; PAYMENT OF TAX.
   (A)   On or after January 1 of each year, but not later than March 1 of any
such year, all banks whose principal offices are located within the county, but
outside any incorporated town in the county, shall prepare and file with the
Commissioner of the Revenue a return as provided by VA Code § 58.1-1207, in
duplicate, which shall set forth the tax on net capital computed pursuant to VA
Code §§ 58.1-1200 through 58.1-1217. The Commissioner of the Revenue shall
certify a copy for such filing of the bank’s return and schedule and shall
forthwith transmit such certified copy to the State Department of Taxation.
   (B)   In the event that the principal office of a bank is located outside
the boundaries of this county or within any town located herein, and such bank
has branch offices located within this county, in addition to the filing
requirements set forth in subsection (A) above, any bank conducting such branch
business shall file with the Commissioner of the Revenue a copy of the real
estate deduction schedule, apportionment and other items which are required by
VA Code §§ 58.1-1207 and 58.1-1211. Each bank, on or before June 1 of each
year, shall pay into the County Treasurer’s office all taxes imposed pursuant
to this article.
(Prior Code, § 15-85) (Ord. passed 6-4-1980)
§ 15-86 PENALTY FOR FAILURE TO COMPLY WITH ARTICLE.
   Any bank which fails to file a return or pay the tax required by this
article or fails to comply with any other provision of this article shall be,
subject to a penalty of 5% of the tax due. If the Commissioner of the Revenue
is satisfied that such failure is due to providential or other good cause, such
return and payment shall be accepted exclusive of such penalty, but with
interest determined in accordance with VA Code § 58.1-15.
(Prior Code, § 15-86) (Ord. passed 6-4-1980)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions applicable to state bank franchise tax, see VA Code §
58.1-1216
§§ 15-87—15-96 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VII. TRANSIENT OCCUPANCY TAX
§ 15-97 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this article, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BOARDINGHOUSE. A lodginghouse at which meals are provided.
   HOTEL. An establishment that provides lodging and usually meals.
   MOTEL. An establishment which provides lodging and parking and in which the
rooms are usually accessible from an outdoor parking area.
   OCCUPANT. Any person occupying any unit.
   TRAVEL CAMPGROUND. An establishment which provides lots or spaces for the
purpose of overnight placement of travel trailers and recreational vehicles.
   UNIT. Any room or space in a hotel, motel, boardinghouse or travel
campground which is meant to be occupied by any person or vehicle for a fee.
(Prior Code, § 15-97) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
Cross-reference:
   Definitions and rules of construction generally, see §
1-2
§ 15-98 IMPOSED; EXEMPTIONS.
   Pursuant to authority contained in VA Code § 58.1-3819, a transient
occupancy tax is hereby imposed and levied by the county upon each and every
hotel, motel, boardinghouse and travel campground, in the amount of 2% of the
amount of the charge for the occupancy for any unit occupied. Such tax shall
not apply to units rented, for continuous occupancy by the same individual or
group for 30 or more days.
(Prior Code, § 15-98) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
§ 15-99 COLLECTION.
   It shall be the duty of every person who provides units, in acting as the
tax collecting medium or agency for the county, to collect from the occupant,
for the use of the county, the tax imposed and levied by this article at the
time of collecting the charge for a unit.
(Prior Code, § 15-99) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
§ 15-100 REPORT AND REMITTANCE.
   (A)   Taxes collected pursuant to §
15-99 during each calendar month shall be reported by the person providing the
units to the County Treasurer.
   (B)   Such person shall remit the amount of tax shown by such report on or
before the last day of the calendar month next following the month so reported.
The required report shall be in the form prescribed by the County Treasurer.
(Prior Code, § 15-100) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
§ 15-101 COLLECTOR’S RECORDS.
   Each person collecting taxes pursuant to §
15-99 shall keep complete records showing all charges imposed for units, the
daily charge made for each unit occupied, the date for which the charge is
made, the date of payment thereof and the amount of tax imposed under this
article. Such records shall be kept open for inspection by the duly authorized
agents of the county during regular business hours, and the duly authorized
agents shall have the right, power and authority to make transcripts thereof
during such time.
(Prior Code, § 15-101) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
§ 15-102 COLLECTOR’S COMMISSION.
   There is hereby allowed a commission, in the form of a deduction from the
taxes remitted pursuant to this article of 3% of the taxes due under this
article to the county, for the services provided the county in collecting and
administering the tax. In no event shall this commission be allowed if the
taxes due under this article are delinquent.
(Prior Code, § 15-102) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code § 58.1-3819
§ 15-103 DUTIES OF TREASURER.
   The County Treasurer shall collect the taxes imposed and levied by this
article and pay such taxes into the general fund of the county.
(Prior Code, § 15-103) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
§ 15-104 OCCUPANT’S FAILURE TO PAY TAX; VIOLATIONS OF ARTICLE BY UNIT
PROVIDERS.
   Any occupant of any unit failing, refusing or neglecting to pay the tax
imposed and levied by this article, and any person providing a unit who
violates the provisions of this article, and any officer, agent or employee of
any person providing such units who violates the provisions of this article,
shall be guilty of a Class 4 misdemeanor.
(Prior Code, § 15-104) (Ord. passed 7-12-1985)
Cross-reference:
   Penalty for Class 4 misdemeanor, see §
1-10
§§ 15-105—15-114 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VIII. TAX ON PROBATE OF WILL OR GRANT OF ADMINISTRATION
§ 15-115 IMPOSED.
   There is hereby imposed a tax on the probate of every will or grant of
administration in the county, which tax shall be equal to one-third of the
state tax on such probate or grant of administration.
(Prior Code, § 15-115) (Res. passed 8-1-1960)

§ 15-116 COLLECTION.
   The tax imposed by this article shall be collected by the Clerk of the

county. The Clerk shall be compensated for such service in the amount of 5% of

meeting of the Board of Supervisors in January of each year, present a bill for
his or her compensation under this section for the previous year. Such
compensation shall be paid to the Clerk from the general fund of the county.

ARTICLE IX. RECORDATION TAX
§ 15-127 IMPOSED.
   There is hereby imposed a recordation tax, in an amount equal to one-third
of the amount of the state recordation tax, upon the first recordation of each
taxable instrument in the county. No tax shall be imposed under this section
when the state recordation tax is $0.50.
(Prior Code, § 15-127) (Ord. passed 3-4-1959)
Statutory reference:
   Authority, see VA Code §§ 58.1-814 and 58.1-3800
§ 15-128 COMPUTATION WHEN PROPERTY LOCATED ONLY PARTIALLY IN COUNTY.
   The tax imposed by this article upon a deed or other instrument which
conveys, covers or relates to property located only partially within the county
shall be computed and collected only with respect to that portion of the
property located in the county.
(Prior Code, § 15-128)
Statutory reference:
   Similar provisions, see VA Code § 58.1-3801
§ 15-129 COLLECTION.
   The tax imposed by this article shall be collected by the Clerk of the
Circuit Court of the county, who shall pay the same into the treasury of the
county. The Clerk shall be compensated for such service in the amount of 5% of
the amount collected and remitted. The Clerk shall at the first regular meeting
of the Board of Supervisors in January of each year present a bill for his or
her compensation, under this section, for the previous year. Such compensation
shall be paid to the Clerk from the general fund of the county.
(Prior Code, § 15-129) (Ord. passed 3-4-1959; Res. passed 1-4-1961)

ARTICLE X. MINERAL SEVERANCE LICENSE TAX
DIVISION 1. COAL SEVERANCE LICENSE TAX
§ 15-139 STATUTORY AUTHORITY.
   The coal severance license tax portions of this division are adopted
pursuant to VA Code Title 58.1, Chapter 37.1 (§§ 58.1-3740 et seq.) and all
other applicable sections of VA Code Title 58.1, Chapters 37 and 39, as
amended, whether or not the specific section is cited herein. Such adoption is
by reference and is inclusive, including all tax collection and lien
enforcement provisions provided by state law. Any and all additional and
applicable sections of VA Code Title 58.1, Chapters 37, 37.1 and 39, as
amended, including, but not limited to, VA Code § 58.1-3703.1, are hereby
adopted and incorporated herein by reference. Any amendments to any applicable
sections of VA Code Title 58.1, Chapters 37, 37.1 and 39, as amended, shall be
deemed to be incorporated into this division when they become effective as if
they were separately adopted.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-140 EFFECTIVE DATE OF AMENDMENTS.
   (A)   As it applies to coal severance license taxes of this division,
including the general provisions in subsection (C) below, revises and replaces
previous ordinances enacted under authority of VA Code §§ 58.1-3712 and 58.1-
3713, as applied to persons engaged in the business of severing coal from the
earth (Prior Coal Severance License Tax Statutes). These amendments are
intended to reflect changes in the law set forth in VA Code §§ 58.1-3740 et
seq. and associated statutory provisions enacted by the Virginia General
Assembly in 2013. This Division 1 shall be effective as of July 1, 2013. This
Division 1 is intended to be applied in accordance with the terms herein. Past
administrative practices in applying prior ordinances enacted pursuant to VA
Code §§ 58.1-3712, 58.1-3713, 58.1-3713.3 and 58.1-3713.4 shall not apply in
interpreting such provisions of this article.
   (B)   All unpaid taxes authorized by the Prior Coal Severance License Tax
Statutes shall remain due and payable.
   (C)   All persons having a valid mineral severance license granted pursuant
to the county’s previously enacted ordinances under the Prior Coal Severance
License Tax Statutes shall be deemed to have a license pursuant to this article
until such time as such licenses must be renewed as provided herein.
   (D)   The penalties for violations of the county’s previously enacted
ordinances under the Prior Coal Severance License Tax Statutes prior to the
effective date shall remain applicable and in full force and effect.
   (E)   All assessments and collections previously made pursuant to the Prior
Coal Severance License Tax Statutes prior to the effective date shall remain
applicable, and are hereby affirmed and ratified pursuant to appropriate
statutory authority.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-141 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this division, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning, unless
otherwise defined by state law.
   COAL. Any mineral deposit composed predominantly of hydrocarbons in a solid
state.
   COAL PRODUCER. The meaning set forth in VA Code § 58.1-3740.
   ECONOMIC INTEREST. The meaning set forth in VA Code § 58.1-3740.
   GROSS RECEIPTS. The meaning set forth in VA Code § 58.1-3740.
   NON-LOCAL COAL TRANSPORTATION AND PROCESSING COSTS. The meaning set forth in
VA Code § 58.1-3740.
   SEVERING, SEVERANCE AND SEVERED WITH REGARD TO COAL. The taking of any coal
from any land, soil, slag piles or any other source situated in the county in
any manner whatsoever.
   SMALL MINE. The meaning set forth in VA Code § 58.1-3740.
   UTILIZED or UTILIZE. To put to beneficial use for such purposes as making
coke, facility heating, power generation, machinery operation, equipment
operation and similar uses.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-142 TAX LEVIED.
   (A)   A license tax is hereby levied and imposed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-
3741(A) on every coal producer that sells or utilizes coal severed from the
earth within the county. The rate of tax for the sale or utilization of coal
from small mines shall be three-fourths of 1% of the gross receipts from the
sale or utilization of such coal by the coal producer. The rate of tax for all
other coal shall be 1% of the gross receipts from the sale or utilization of
such coal by the coal producer.
   (B)   In addition to the tax imposed in subsection (A) above, a license tax
is hereby levied and imposed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3741(B) on every coal
producer that sells or utilizes coal severed from the earth within the county.
The rate of tax for the sale or utilization of coal from small mines shall be
three-fourths of 1% of the gross receipts from the sale or utilization of such
coal by the coal producer. The rate of tax for all other coal shall be 1% of
the gross receipts from the sale or utilization of such coal by the coal
producer.
   (C)   The foregoing taxes are hereby levied and imposed in addition to all
other taxes and fees of every kind now imposed by law upon every coal producer.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
DIVISION 2. GAS AND OIL SEVERANCE LICENSE TAXES
§ 15-152 STATUTORY AUTHORITY.
   The gas and oil severance license tax portions of this division are adopted
pursuant to VA Code §§ 58.1-3712, 58.1-3713, 58.1-3713.3 and 58.1-3713.4 (the
Gas Severance License Tax Statutes) and all other applicable sections of VA
Code Title 58.1, Chapters 37 and 39, as amended, whether or not the specific
section is cited herein. Such adoption is by reference and is inclusive,
including all tax collection and lien enforcement provisions provided by state
law. Any and all additional and applicable sections of VA Code Title 58.1,
Chapters 37 and 39, as amended, including, but not limited to, VA Code § 58.1-
3703.1, are hereby adopted and incorporated herein by reference. Any amendments
to any applicable sections of VA Code Title 58.1, Chapter 37 and Chapter 39, as
amended, shall be deemed to be incorporated into this division when they become
effective as if they were separately adopted.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-153 EFFECTIVE DATE OF AMENDMENTS.
   (A)   As it applies to gas and oil severance license taxes, this division,
including the general provisions in subsection (C) below, amends the county
coal, gas and oil severance license tax ordinance adopted on June 19, 2012,
which was enacted under authority of the Gas Severance License Tax Statutes,
being VA Code § 58.1-3713, and effective as of January 1, 2008. These
amendments shall not alter that prior effective date. This division is intended
to be applied in accordance with the terms stated herein. Past administrative
practices in applying prior ordinances enacted pursuant to the Gas Severance
License Tax Statutes shall not apply in interpreting this division.
   (B)   All unpaid taxes authorized by the Gas Severance License Tax Statutes
shall remain due and payable.
   (C)   All persons having a valid mineral severance license granted pursuant
to the county’s previously enacted ordinances under the Gas Severance License
Tax Statutes shall be deemed to have a license pursuant to this division until
such time as such licenses must be renewed as provided herein.
   (D)   The penalties for violations of the county’s previously enacted
ordinances under the Gas Severance License Tax Statutes prior to the effective
date shall remain applicable and in full force and effect.
   (E)   All assessments and collections previously made pursuant to the Gas
Severance License Tax Statutes prior to the effective date shall remain
applicable and are hereby affirmed and ratified pursuant to appropriate
statutory authority.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-154 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this division, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning, unless
otherwise defined by state law.
   COALBED METHANE GAS. Occluded natural gas produced from coalbeds and rock
strata associated therewith.
   FAIR MARKET VALUE.
      (1)   In circumstances where the gas or oil is sold by arms-length
transaction between unrelated persons, the sale price of the gas or oil; and
      (2)   In circumstances in which the gas or oil is utilized or sold in a
related party transaction or under other circumstances that indicate that the
sale is not an arms-length transaction, the average sale price received by the
person engaged in the business of severing oil or gas from the earth in arms-
length transactions for the sale of other minerals of comparable quality
produced from a comparable area during the same time frame or, if none, the
sale price for other such minerals of comparable quality as indicated by either
appropriate regional indices or sales by other persons engaged in the severance
of similar minerals within the county or neighboring counties.
   GAS. All natural gas, including, but not limited to, coalbed methane gas,
whether hydrocarbon or non-hydrocarbon or any combination or mixture thereof,
including hydrocarbons, hydrogen sulfide, helium, carbon dioxide, nitrogen,
hydrogen, casing head gas and all other fluids not defined as oil herein.
   GROSS RECEIPTS. Except in the case of persons engaging in the production and
operation of severing gases from the earth in connection with coal mining, the
fair market value of the severed oil or gas measured at the time the oil or gas
is utilized or sold for utilization in the county or at the time the oil or gas
is placed in transit for shipment from the county. When such minerals are
placed in transit for shipment from the county, fair market value may be
reduced by deducting reasonable costs actually incurred by the person engaged
in the business of severing oil or gas from the earth in processing or
transporting the mineral after it is placed in transit for shipment from the
county prior to sale of the mineral. For persons engaging in the production and
operation of severing gases from the earth in connection with coal mining,
GROSS RECEIPTS means the fair market value of the gas measured at the time it
is utilized or sold for utilization in the county or at the time it is placed
in transit for shipment from the county, with no deduction or allowance for
costs. In all circumstances, gross receipts includes the royalty share of the
mineral(s) severed and all minerals subject to a royalty obligation.
   MINERAL or MINERALS. Oil or gas.
   OIL. Natural crude oil or petroleum and other hydrocarbons, regardless of
gravity, which are produced at the well, in liquid form by ordinary production
methods and which are not the result of condensation of gas after it leaves the
underground reservoir.
   OWNER. The owner of a legal or equitable interest in oil or gas at the time
of severance.
   PERSON. Any individual, firm, partnership, limited liability company,
corporation, cooperative, joint venture, association, estate, trust, business
trust, trustee, trustee in bankruptcy, any person acting under a declaration of
trust, executor, administrator, partner, agent, receiver, syndicate, assignee,
or other group or combination acting as a unit, in the plural, as well as in
the singular number.
   PERSON ENGAGED OR ENGAGING IN THE BUSINESS OF SEVERING OIL OR GAS FROM THE
EARTH.
      (1)   Where the minerals are unleased, the owner(s) of such minerals; or
      (2)   Where the minerals are leased, the lessee of the mineral or the
lessee of the right to extract, mine or produce such minerals.
   PLACED IN TRANSIT FOR SHIPMENT FROM THE COUNTY. The point in distribution of
the severed mineral at which the mineral is placed in final shipment from the
county with no additional treatment, processing, compression, handling or
mechanical manipulation to be performed within the county. Except in cases
where gas is produced at the wellhead at sufficient pressure and quality such
that it is not treated in any manner or compressed by mechanical compressor
within the county, gas is not placed in transit for shipment from the county at
the wellhead.
   SEVERING, SEVERANCE AND SEVERED WITH REGARD TO OIL OR GAS. The taking of any
oil or gas from any land, soil, landfill, or any other formation or source
situated in the county in any manner whatsoever.
   SEVERING GASES FROM THE EARTH IN CONNECTION WITH COAL MINING. Producing
coalbed methane gas from wells that directly or indirectly remove gas from:
units or permitted well areas which include coal seams that have been fractured
by current or previous mining activities (GOB wells); and units or permitted
well areas which include coal seams that have been fractured in the absence of
mining (FRAC wells), but where all or some of the fractured coal seams are
within a permitted mine boundary or within the area projected for mining by the
20-year mine plan map for any coal operator.
   UTILIZED OR UTILIZE WITH REGARD TO OIL OR GAS. To put to beneficial use for
such purposes as facility heating, power generation, machinery operation,
equipment operation and similar uses. Utilized minerals include oil or gas that
is severed from the earth within the county and used by the person engaged in
the business of severing oil or gas from the earth (or those acting on his or
her behalf, at his or her direction, or with his or her permission or consent)
in some beneficial manner, in which case, the severed and utilized mineral
shall be deemed to have been sold for the fair market value of such mineral.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-155 TAX LEVIED.
   (A)   A license tax is hereby levied and imposed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-
3712, 1950, as amended, on every person engaged in the business of severing gas
from the earth. Such tax shall be at a rate of 1% of gross receipts.
   (B)   In addition to the taxes levied in subsection (A) above, a license tax
is hereby levied and imposed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3713, 1950, as amended,
on every person engaged in the business of severing gas from the earth. Such
tax shall be at a rate of 1% of gross receipts.
   (C)   In addition to the taxes levied in subsections (A) and (B) above, a
license tax is hereby levied and imposed pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3713.4,
1950, as amended, on every person engaged in the business of severing gas from
the earth. Such tax shall be at a rate of 1% of gross receipts. A license tax
is hereby levied and imposed on every person engaged in the business of
severing oil from the earth. Such tax shall be at a rate of one-half of 1% of
gross receipts. mThe foregoing taxes are hereby levied and imposed in addition
to all other taxes and fees of every kind now imposed by law upon every person
engaged in the business of severing oil or gas from the earth.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§§ 15-156—15-164 RESERVED.
DIVISION 3. GENERAL PROVISIONS APPLICABLE TO COAL, GAS AND OIL SEVERANCE
LICENSE TAXES
§ 15-165 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this division, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning, unless
otherwise defined by state law.
   CLOSELY-HELD CORPORATION. A corporation not publicly traded and having 20 or
fewer shareholders.
   COMMON CARRIER. Any person involved in any phase of the transportation of
coal, oil or gas within the county or from the county. This includes, but is
not limited to, the receiving, collection or assembly of coal, oil or gas for
conveyance from one mode of transportation to another or to the same mode of
transportation, as well as the actual movement of the coal, oil or gas in
shipment.
   MINING OPERATION. Any act or activity which results in the severing of coal,
oil or gas from the earth.
   PERSON. Any individual, firm, partnership, limited liability company,
corporation, cooperative, joint venture, association, estate, trust, business
trust, trustee, trustee in bankruptcy, any person acting under a declaration of
trust, executor, administrator, partner, agent, receiver, syndicate, assignee
or other group or combination acting as a unit, in the plural, as well as in
the singular number.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-166 LICENSE GENERALLY.
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any coal producer or any person to engage in
the business of severing coal, oil or gas from the earth within the county or
to cause others to sever coal, oil or gas from the earth within the county,
unless the coal producer or person engaging in the business of severing coal,
oil or gas from the earth has first obtained a current license to do so issued
by the Commissioner of the Revenue.
   (B)   Every coal producer and every person engaged in the business of
severing oil or gas from the earth shall file with the Commissioner of Revenue
an application for a license for each of such coal producer’s or such person’s
mining operations in the county. Every application shall be signed by each such
coal producer or person or an authorized representative of such coal producer
or person. In connection with any such application, the coal producer or the
person engaged in the business of severing oil or gas from the earth shall
provide such information as the Commissioner of Revenue may require.
   (C)   (1)   Every coal producer and every person engaged in the business of
severing oil or gas from the earth that did not have a license to sever coal,
oil or gas in the county in the previous license tax year shall file an
application as provided herein prior to beginning any severance of coal, oil or
gas in the county.
      (2)   Every coal producer and every person engaged in the business of
severing oil or gas from the earth that had a license or licenses to sever
coal, oil or gas in the county in the previous license tax year shall file an
application for the renewal of such license or licenses on or before March 1 of
the current license tax year. In such case, the existing license shall remain
in effect until the new license is issued. Issuance of a new license may be
conditioned upon receipt by the Commissioner of Revenue of a written report
from the County Treasurer documenting such person’s payment of any license
taxes due or an arrangement for the payment of any license taxes.
      (3)   The Commissioner of Revenue may grant an extension of time in which
to file an application for a license or renewal thereof, for reasonable cause.
The extension may be conditioned upon the timely payment of a reasonable
estimate of the appropriate tax. Any such estimated tax is subject to
adjustment to the correct tax at the end of the extension, together with
interest from the due date until the date paid and, if the estimate submitted
with the extension is found to be unreasonable under the circumstances, with a
penalty of 10% of the portion paid after the due date.
   (D)   When the required application has been made, the Commissioner of
Revenue shall issue to each applicant who has met all of the requirements of
this article a separate license for each mining operation within the county,
which license shall not be transferable.
   (E)   No license shall be issued or reissued under this section to a person
who owns an interest in a mining operation conducted by a person owing
delinquent taxes at the time the application is submitted, or to a person who
owes delinquent taxes. When such facts are known to the Commissioner of
Revenue, he or she may, at his or her election, hold the hearing provided for
in subsection (F) below. An arrangement for payment of delinquent taxes made by
the County Treasurer may be treated as payment for the purposes of this
section.
   (F)   Whenever any person fails to comply with any provision of this
division, the Commissioner of Revenue may hold a hearing after giving such
person ten days’ notice, in writing, specifying the time and place of hearing
and requiring the person to show cause why his or her license should not be
revoked or suspended or his or her application for renewal of his or her
license should not be denied. The Commissioner of Revenue may revoke or suspend
or deny reissuance of any one or more of the licenses held by such person.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-167 RETURNS.
   Every coal producer and every person engaged in the business of severing oil
or gas from the earth required to pay any of the taxes imposed by this article
shall, on or before the twentieth day of each month, transmit to the
Commissioner of Revenue, upon a form furnished by the Commissioner, a completed
return showing such information as the Commissioner of Revenue may require,
including the quantities of coal, oil and gas produced from each mining
operation; the gross receipts from all coal, oil and gas severed from each
mining operation during the immediately preceding calendar month; and any
deductions that have been applied in calculating gross receipts. At the request
of the Commissioner of Revenue, coal producers and persons engaging in the
business of severing oil or gas shall provide the names and addresses of any
owners or other persons participating in each mining operation, any persons who
are members of an affiliated group of which the operator is a member and to
whom the coal, oil or gas was sold or placed into transit for shipment from the
county, and all persons having an economic interest in the mining operation. In
the event that any date on which a return is to be filed falls upon a Saturday,
Sunday, legal holiday or other date on which the county courthouse is closed,
then the time for the filing of such return shall be extended until the next
day that the Commissioner of Revenue’s office is open for business. This return
shall be made under oath and subject to the penalty for perjury. The
Commissioner of Revenue shall transmit to the County Treasurer forthwith all
records related to the taxes owed by and the payments received from each coal
producer and each person engaged in the business of severing gas or oil from
the earth.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-168 PAYMENT OF TAX; PENALTY AND INTEREST ON DELINQUENCIES.
   (A)   At the time of transmitting the return required by § 15-167 to the
Commissioner of Revenue, the coal producer or person engaged in the business of
severing oil or gas from the earth shall remit to the County Treasurer
therewith the amount of tax due under the applicable provisions of this
article. Failure to remit such tax by the deadline for filing the return
required by § 15-167 shall cause such tax to become delinquent.
   (B)   A penalty of 10% of the tax may be imposed upon the failure to file an
application for a license or the failure to pay the required tax by the
appropriate due dates set forth in this division. Only the late filing penalty
shall be imposed by the Commissioner of the Revenue if both the application and
tax payment are late; however, both penalties may be assessed if the
Commissioner of the Revenue determines that the taxpayer has a history of non-
compliance. In the case of an assessment of additional tax made by the
Commissioner of Revenue, if the application and, if applicable, the return were
made in good faith and the understatement of the tax was not due to any fraud
or reckless or intentional disregard of the law by the taxpayer, there shall be
no late payment penalty assessed with the additional tax. If any assessment of
tax by the Commissioner of Revenue is not paid within 30 days, the County
Treasurer may impose a 10% late payment penalty. If the failure to file or pay
was not the fault of the taxpayer, the penalties shall not be imposed, or if
imposed, shall be abated by the County Treasurer. In order to demonstrate lack
of fault, the taxpayer must show that he or she acted responsibly and that the
failure was due to events beyond his or her control.
      (1)   ACTED RESPONSIBLY means that the taxpayer exercised the level of
reasonable care that a prudent person would exercise under the circumstances in
determining the filing obligations for the business; and the taxpayer undertook
significant steps to avoid or mitigate the failure, such as requesting
appropriate extensions (where applicable), attempting to prevent a foreseeable
impediment, acting to remove an impediment once it occurred and promptly
rectifying a failure once the impediment was removed or the failure discovered.
      (2)   EVENTS BEYOND THE TAXPAYER’S CONTROL include, but are not limited
to, the unavailability of records due to fire or other casualty; the
unavoidable absence (such as, due to death or serious illness) of the person
with the sole responsibility for tax compliance; or the taxpayer’s reasonable
reliance in good faith upon erroneous written information from the assessing
official who was aware of the relevant facts relating to the taxpayer’s
business when he or she provided the erroneous information.
   (C)   Interest shall be charged on the late payment of the tax from the due
date until the date paid without regard to fault or other reason for the late
payment. Whenever an assessment of additional or omitted tax by the
Commissioner of Revenue is found to be erroneous, all interest and any
penalties charged and collected on the amount of the assessment found to be
erroneous shall be refunded together with interest on the refund from the date
of payment or the due date, whichever is later. Interest shall be paid on the
refund of any tax from the date of payment or due date, whichever is later,
whether attributable to an amended return or other reason. However, no interest
shall be paid on a refund or charged on a late payment; provided the refund or
the late payment is made not more than 30 days from the date of the payment
that created the refund or the due date of the tax, whichever is later.
Interest charged on any late payment or paid on any refund shall be calculated
at the same rate charged under VA Code § 58.1-3916. No interest shall accrue on
an adjustment of estimated tax liability to actual liability at the conclusion
of a base year.
   (D)   The County Treasurer and the Commissioner of Revenue shall reconcile
their records monthly concerning the identities of taxpayers, amounts received,
outstanding taxes due, and, if applicable, any arrangements made by the County
Treasurer for payment of delinquent taxes.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-169 PROCEDURE WHEN COAL PRODUCER OR PERSON ENGAGED IN THE BUSINESS OF
SEVERING OIL OR GAS FROM THE EARTH FAILS TO MAKE RETURN OR MAKES INCORRECT OR
FALSE RETURN.
   In the event any coal producer or person engaged in the business of severing
oil or gas from the earth fails to make a return as provided by this division,
the Commissioner of Revenue shall give such coal producer or such person ten
days’ notice in writing requiring such coal producer or such person to appear
before him or her, with such books, records and papers as the Commissioner of
Revenue may require relating to the business of such coal producer or such
person for such taxable period, and the Commissioner of Revenue may require
such coal producer or such person or the agents and employees of such coal
producer or such person to give testimony or to answer interrogatories under
oath respecting such mining or extracting of coal, oil or gas, or the failure
to make a return thereof as provided in this article. If, after being provided
with the opportunity to supply such information, such coal producer or such
person still fails to make a return or refuses to permit an examination of his
or its books, records or papers, or to appear and answer questions within the
scope of such investigation, the Commissioner of Revenue is hereby authorized
to make an estimate of gross receipts for all such coal, oil or gas severed by
or at the direction of such coal producer or such person, and to assess the
appropriate tax, plus penalties and interest in accordance with § 15-168, based
upon such information as may be available to him or her. The County Treasurer
may issue a warrant for the collection of any such taxes and penalties so found
to be due. The assessment so made shall be deemed prima facie correct. In
addition, the Commissioner of Revenue may, upon reasonable notice, assess taxes
for such mining operation against any other person liable for the tax.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-170 PROCEDURE WHEN COAL PRODUCER OR PERSON ENGAGED IN THE BUSINESS OF
SEVERING OIL OR GAS FROM THE EARTH CEASES OPERATIONS.
   If the holder of a license issued under this article ceases to conduct a
mining operation, the license shall thereupon expire and such license holder
shall inform the Commissioner of Revenue in writing within 30 days thereafter
that he or she has ceased to conduct such mining operation. A copy of such
report, upon receipt thereof, shall be forwarded to the County Treasurer.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-171 MAINTENANCE OF RECORDS.
   (A)   (1)   Every person who is assessable with a license tax under this
division or who is a common carrier of coal, oil or gas shall keep sufficient
records, including, but not limited to, records showing the source and quantity
of, and gross receipts from, the coal, oil and gas which he or she has produced
or transported, or for which he or she has received some economic benefit, to
enable the Commissioner of Revenue to verify the correctness of the tax paid
for the license months or years assessable and to enable the Commissioner of
Revenue to ascertain what is the correct amount of tax that was assessable for
each of those months or years.
      (2)   All such records, books of accounts, and other information shall be
open to inspection and examination by the Commissioner of Revenue in order to
allow the Commissioner of Revenue to establish whether a particular receipt is
directly attributable to the taxable privilege exercised within the county.
      (3)   The Commissioner of Revenue shall provide such persons with the
option to conduct the audit in such person’s local business office within the
county, if the records are maintained there. In the event the records are
maintained outside the county, copies of the appropriate books and records
shall be sent to the Commissioner’s office upon demand.
   (B)   Any common carrier involved in the transportation of coal, oil or gas
within or from the county shall submit, upon request, to the Commissioner of
Revenue records showing the source and quantity of, and, if purchased, the
price paid for, all coal, oil or gases which the common carrier acquired or
transported during the applicable time periods. This information may be made
available to any other political subdivision in which the coal, oil or gas may
have been severed.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-172 DISTRIBUTION OF TAXES COLLECTED.
   (A)   The taxes collected pursuant to this division shall be paid and
distributed as provided by state law. Any taxes not distributed according to
specific provisions of law shall be paid into the general fund of the county.
   (B)   In the event that a taxpayer is issued a refund of severance license
taxes paid pursuant to this division, the recipients of the revenue from such
severance license taxes shall be proportionately liable for such refund based
on their respective percentages of the original distribution of such revenue.
The County Treasurer is hereby authorized to off-set such liability for any
such refund against any future distribution of severance license tax revenues
paid pursuant to this division.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-173 COAL AND GAS ROAD IMPROVEMENT ADVISORY COMMITTEE GENERALLY.
   Pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3713, there is hereby established a Coal and Gas
Road Improvement Advisory Committee to be composed of four members as follows:
a member of the Board of Supervisors of the county appointed by the Board of
Supervisors; a representative of the Virginia Department of Transportation; and
two citizens of the county connected with the coal and gas industries, and to
be appointed for a term of four years by the Chief Judge of the Circuit Court.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-174 COAL AND GAS ROAD IMPROVEMENT PLANS.
   (A)   Pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3713, the Coal and Gas Road Improvement
Advisory Committee shall develop, on or before July 1 of each year, a plan for
improvement of roads during the following fiscal year.
   (B)   Such plan must have the approval of three members of the Committee and
shall be submitted to the Board of Supervisors of the county for approval. The
Board of Supervisors may approve or disapprove such plan, but may make no
changes without the approval of three members of the Committee.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-175 USE OF COUNTY FUNDS FOR COAL AND GAS ROAD IMPROVEMENTS IN TOWNS OR
CITY.
   The Board of Supervisors may, in its discretion, and when permitted by
applicable state law, elect to improve city and town roads with its funds, if
consent of the city or town council is obtained.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-176 VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES.
   (A)   (1)   The following persons shall be guilty of a Class 1 misdemeanor:
         (a)   Any person who engages in the business of severing coal, oil or
gas from the earth in this county without first obtaining a license or after a
license has been suspended or revoked;
         (b)   Each officer or director of a corporation that engages in the
business of severing coal, oil or gas from the earth in this county without
first obtaining a license or after a license has been suspended or revoked;
provided that such officer or director had actual or constructive knowledge
that the corporation was engaging in the business of severing coal, oil or gas
from the earth in this county without first obtaining a license or after a
license had been suspended or revoked;
         (c)   Each shareholder of a closely-held corporation that engages in
the business of severing coal, oil or gas from the earth in this county without
first obtaining a license or after a license has been suspended or revoked;
provided that such shareholder had actual or constructive knowledge that the
corporation was engaging in the business of severing coal, oil or gas from the
earth in this county without first obtaining a license or after a license had
been suspended or revoked; or
         (d)   Any person who violates any provision of this division.
      (2)   Each day of violation shall constitute a separate offense. No
person shall be convicted under the provisions of subsections (A)(1)(a) and (A)
(1)(c) above who shall have objected to the conduct of the mining operation in
writing to the president or secretary of such corporation and forwarded a copy
of this objection to the Commissioner of the Revenue.
   (B)   (1)   It shall be unlawful for any person:
         (a)   To fail to keep the records required by this division or fail to
make such records available as herein required;
         (b)   Willfully to fail to pay, collect or truthfully account for and
pay any license tax herein imposed; or
         (c)   Willfully to attempt in any manner to evade or defeat any such
license tax or the payment thereof.
      (2)   Each day of violation shall constitute a separate offense.
   (C)   Violations under this section shall be Class 1 misdemeanors, and shall
be punishable by a fine not to exceed $2,500 for each day of violation and
confinement in the county jail for not more than 12 months, either or both in
the discretion of the court or jury trying the case. Conviction of a second
offense under this section shall, in addition to a fine not to exceed $2,500,
require confinement in the county jail for not less than ten days nor more than
12 months.
   (D)   Any penalty imposed for violation of this section shall be in addition
to the civil remedies or penalties provided for by law.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-177 LIMITATIONS AND EXTENSIONS OF ASSESSMENTS AND COLLECTIONS OF TAX.
   (A)   Where, before the expiration of the time prescribed for the assessment
of any license tax imposed pursuant to this division, both the Commissioner of
Revenue and the taxpayer have consented in writing to its assessment after such
time, the tax may be assessed at any time prior to the expiration of the period
agreed upon. The period so agreed upon may be extended by subsequent agreements
in writing made before the expiration of the period previously agreed upon.
   (B)   Notwithstanding VA Code § 58.1-3903, the Commissioner of Revenue shall
assess the license tax omitted because of fraud or failure to apply for a
license for the current license tax year and the six preceding license tax
years.
   (C)   The period for collecting any local license tax shall not expire prior
to the period specified in VA Code § 58.1-3940, two years after the date of
assessment if the period for assessment has been extended pursuant to this
section, two years after the final determination of an appeal for which
collection has been stayed pursuant to § 15-178(B) or (D), or two years after
the final decision in a court application pursuant to VA Code § 58.1-3984 or a
similar law for which collection has been stayed, whichever is later.
(Ord. passed 6-18-2013)
§ 15-178 ADMINISTRATIVE APPEALS TO THE COMMISSIONER OF REVENUE.
   (A)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      AMOUNT IN DISPUTE. When used with respect to taxes due or assessed, the
amount specifically identified in the administrative appeal or application for
judicial review as disputed by the party filing such appeal or application.
      APPEALABLE EVENT. An increase in the assessment of a license tax payable
by a taxpayer, the denial of a refund, or the assessment of a license tax where
none previously was assessed, arising out of the Commissioner of Revenue’s
examination of records, financial statements, books of account or other
information for the purpose of determining the correctness of an assessment;
determination regarding the rate or classification applicable to the licensable
business; assessment of a license tax when no return has been filed by the
taxpayer; or denial of an application for correction of erroneous assessment
attendant to the filing of an amended application for license.
