ARTICLE I. INTRODUCTORY PROVISIONS
§ 17-1 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of the county addressing and road naming ordinance is to protect
the safety and welfare of the general public through the orderly assignment of
addresses to facilitate the location of individual dwellings and businesses by
emergency response personnel.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-2 ENACTMENT AND AUTHORITY.
   There is hereby established and adopted a detailed, permanent and uniform
addressing system, pursuant to authority of VA Code § 15.2-2019, empowering the
local government to name roads.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-3 SHORT TITLE.
   This chapter shall be known as the “Road Naming and Addressing Ordinance of
Lee County, Virginia” and may be referred to as this chapter.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-4 TERRITORIAL JURISDICTION.
   The road naming and addressing policies set forth in this chapter shall be
applicable for all of the unincorporated areas of the county.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-5 INCORPORATED AREAS.
   Any incorporated area within the county that is being provided emergency
dispatch services by the county’s Communications/E-911 Center, is requested to
adhere to the road naming and addressing policies set forth in this chapter,
and which may require the adoption of a compatible ordinance by its governing
board.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-6 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURE. Any structure that is a primary place of living,
working, playing or worshiping.
   ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURE NUMBER. The numerical portion of the street address,
as assigned by the E-911 Coordinator or his or her designee, in accordance with
the official road name map book of the county.
   ADDRESSING POINT OF ORIGIN. The end of a named road designated for the start
of addressable structure numbers.
   COMMUNICATIONS/E-911 CENTER. The public safety answering point at the county
that is responsible for answering E-911 calls.
   MOBILE HOME PARK. A lot or parcel on which is located, or which is arranged
or equipped for the accommodation of, two or more manufactured homes for
dwelling use with spaces for such available for rent or lease.
   OFFICIAL ROAD NAME MAP BOOK. Map book adopted by the Board of Supervisors
denoting the names of each named road in the county.
   ORDINANCE ADMINISTRATOR. The Board of Supervisors or its designee.
   PRIVATE ROAD. Any road which is not maintained by a governmental entity or
agency through the use of public funds.
   PUBLIC ROAD. Any road which is maintained by a governmental entity or agency
through the use of public funds.
   STREET ADDRESS. An unique identifier for each addressable structure within
the county. The minimum adequate street address shall be defined as the
assigned addressable structure number and the officially adopted road name.
Where required by this chapter, the STREET ADDRESS shall also include the
assigned unit designator.
   UNIT DESIGNATOR. The portion of the street address used to distinguish
individual units within the same addressable structure.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-7 CONFLICT WITH OTHER LAWS.
   (A)   All other ordinances or parts of ordinance not specifically in
conflict herewith are hereby continued in force and effect, but all such
ordinances or parts of ordinances in conflict herewith are hereby repealed.
   (B)   Where the provisions of this chapter are higher or more restrictive
than those imposed by any other applicable law or regulation, such higher or
more restrictive provisions shall apply.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-8 SEVERABILITY.
   Should any section, subsection, sentence, clause, phrase or provision of
this chapter be declared unconstitutional or invalid by a court of competent
jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity of the ordinance in
its entirety or of any part thereof other than that so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-9—17-18 RESERVED.
ARTICLE II. ADDRESSING MAP BOOK
§ 17-19 OFFICIAL ROAD NAME MAP BOOK.
   (A)   The road name map book shall be entitled “Official Road Name Map Book,
Lee County, Virginia.”
   (B)   The effective date of said map book shall be entered here upon
approval of the map book by the Board of Supervisors upon completion of the
road naming process. Said map book shall hereby be adopted as the official road
name map book of the county.
   (C)   All county addresses assigned shall be assigned in accordance with
this map book.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-20 MAINTENANCE AND STORAGE.
   The official road name map book shall be kept on file with the County E-911
Coordinator. This map book shall be maintained and updated digitally with a
master hard copy in print at all times.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-21—17-29 RESERVED.
ARTICLE III. NUMBERING SYSTEM
§ 17-30 UNIFORMITY OF THE SYSTEM.
   A main road point of origin linear addressing scheme utilizing U.S. Highway
58 will be used. Addresses on U.S. Highway 58 will begin where U.S. Highway 58
enters the county in the west, starting with an address of 100. Addresses will
generally flow away from U.S. Highway 58. All roads that are officially
designated on the addressing map book, whether public or private, shall be
numbered uniformly and consecutively along the roadway centerline. Numbers
shall be assigned along the entirety of all named roads.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-31 ROAD NAMING CRITERIA.
   (A)   All public roads shall be named, have road name signs installed and
all addressable structures shall be numbered.
   (B)   Private roads shall be named, have road name signs installed and all
addressable structures shall be numbered, if:
      (1)   Three or more addressable structures exist on the private road; or
      (2)   The private road is longer than 1,000 feet and has at least one
addressable structure along the road.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-32 NUMBERING METHOD.
   (A)   A set of numbers consisting of a three-, four- or five-digit natural
number, called an addressable structure number, shall be assigned at the rate
of 1,000 addresses per mile; resulting in an address pair every 10.56 feet; 500
addresses per side of road, per mile.
   (B)   Odd addressable structure numbers shall be assigned to the left side
of the road moving away from the addressing point of origin on the said road.
Even addressable structure numbers shall be assigned to the right side of the
road moving away from the addressing point of origin on the said road.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-33 DEAD-END ROADS.
   (A)   Address numbers on all dead-end roads shall begin with the point of
address number origin at the intersecting road and increase towards the dead-
end.
   (B)   Address numbers on cul-de-sacs shall begin with the point of address
number origin at the intersecting road and increase towards the cul-de-sac
circle. When entering the cu-de-sac circle, addresses will continue to increase
counterclockwise, bearing to the right, around the cul-de-sac circle.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-34 BEGINNING ADDRESS NUMBER.
   Each road’s point of origin shall begin with the number 100.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-35—17-43 RESERVED.
ARTICLE IV. ADDRESSING SYSTEM
§ 17-44 METHOD OF ASSIGNING A NUMBER.
   (A)   An even and an odd number will be available for addressing for every
10.56 feet of road frontage throughout the county. There will be 1,000 possible
addresses per mile; 500 per side of road.
   (B)   The address number will be assigned where the addressable structure’s
driveway intersects the road from which the addressable structure will be
addressed.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-45 CORNER LOTS.
   Addressable structures on corner lots shall be assigned an addressable
structure number where the addressable structure’s driveway intersects a road.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-46 ROAD NAME OF ADDRESS.
   The road name of an address shall be the name of the road from which the
addressable structure is numbered.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-47 REQUIREMENTS OF ROAD NAMING AND NUMBERING.
   If development of a private road or addressable structures along the private
road meets or exceeds the minimum addressable structure or length regulations
(as outlined in §
17-31), said road shall be named and numbered, and addressable structures
readdressed according to the requirements herein.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-48 DUPLEX AND MULTI-FAMILY DWELLINGS.
   One addressable structure number shall be assigned to each addressable
structure whose units share a common roof. Each unit within the addressable
structure shall be assigned a unit designator. Allowed unit designators include
apartment numbers for apartments and numbers for commercial buildings. The unit
designator shall be a number and shall not include alphabetic characters,
except as stated in §
17-49.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-49 ASSIGNING OF UNIT DESIGNATORS.
   Residential unit designators shall be as follows: ground level floor numbers
- #101, #102, #103 and the like, second floor numbers - #201, #202, #203 and
the like. All floor levels are to follow this scheme. Underground floor
designators shall follow the same scheme with the exception of having a “U” for
a prefix, for example #U101, #U102 and the like. This section specifically
applies to multi-family dwellings.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-50 MOBILE HOMES.
   (A)   Mobile homes shall be assigned individual street addresses if not
located within a mobile home development.
   (B)   A mobile home development will receive a single address. Manufactured
housing or mobile homes within mobile home developments will receive lot
numbers. Mobile homes within a mobile home development will have an address
such as: 1345 Spring Road, Lot 1.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-51 RECREATIONAL OR RESORT COMMUNITIES.
   Resort communities or recreational developments that have established
dwelling sites with electrical power hook-ups, or municipal sewage hook-ups, or
phone hook-ups shall be assigned individual street addresses.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-52 ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURES WITH ALLEY VEHICLE MAIN ACCESS.
   Addressable structures with vehicle access from an alley will be addressed
from the road the addressable structure faces. The digital map database of
structures will contain attribute data denoting a vehicle entrance other than
the road from which the structure is addressed.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-53 ADDRESS ASSIGNMENT AFTER THE INITIAL E-911 ROAD NAMING AND ADDRESSING
PROCESS.
   Future addresses shall be assigned by utilizing the following procedure:
   (A)   A resident receives a building permit;
   (B)   The Building Inspector gives the E-911 Coordinator a copy of the
building permit;
   (C)   The E-911 Coordinator assigns an address appropriately; and
   (D)   The E-911 Coordinator informs the resident of their new address in
writing and provides notification to other county departments as needed.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-54—17-62 RESERVED.
ARTICLE V. POSTING REQUIREMENTS FOR ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURES
§ 17-63 TIME CONSTRAINTS.
   Within 90 days after written notification of the assignment of or change of
an addressable structure number, the owner of said addressable structure shall
post the assigned addressable structure number in compliance with the
requirements herein.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-64 NUMBER SPECIFICATIONS.
   All addressable structure numbers shall be constructed of a durable
material. The color shall contrast with the color scheme of the addressable
structure, and if mounted on glass, shall contrast with the background and be
clearly visible. The minimum number size for residential addressable structures
or units shall be four inches in height. The minimum size for all other
addressable structure numbers shall be six inches in height. In all cases, a
number larger than the minimum size may be required where the minimum size does
not provide adequate identification.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-65 POSTING LOCATIONS.
   All numerical identifications must be easily identifiable without
obstruction of view. Any dwelling or business located more than 100 feet from
the roadway and/or not clearly visible from the roadway shall be required to
have numerical posting at both the entrance or driveway and located in close
proximity to the front door or entranceway. A minimum of five feet in posting
height will be required for all dwelling or business identification in close
proximity to the driveway entrance. The post height of three feet will be
required for all entrances that require numerical posting. A mailbox is
acceptable if it is located at the entranceway to the property.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-66 MAINTENANCE OF ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURE NUMBERS.
   Following the posting of the assigned number as required herein, the owner
shall maintain the addressable structure number at all times in compliance with
the requirements of this chapter. Addressable structure numbers and unit
designators, as viewed from the road, shall not be obstructed from view.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-67—17-75 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VI. ROAD NAMING
§ 17-76 APPROVAL OF ROAD NAMES.
   (A)   The Board of Supervisors shall have authority to approve public and
private roads requiring road names.
   (B)   Road names will be approved when the initial road naming process is
complete and an official road name map is presented to and adopted by the
Board.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-77 INITIAL ROAD NAMING PROCEDURE.
   Roads will be named by utilizing the following procedure:
   (A)   Road naming meetings will be advertised and open to the public;
   (B)   Public road naming meetings will be held at familiar and local
locations. No more than one meeting will be held per voting precinct (some
precinct meetings may be combined);
   (C)   After each road naming meeting, citizens that did not attend the
meeting within that (those) precinct(s) will have an additional ten days to
submit their road name suggestions in writing or in person at the County
Administrator’s Office. After the ten-day deadline, citizens may no longer
submit road name suggestions;
   (D)   Up to three road name suggestions per person, per eligible road are
permissible;
   (E)   Road name suggestions will be evaluated and chosen for each road by
the Board of Supervisors. Roads that did not receive a public road name
suggestion will be named to the best ability of the Board of Supervisors;
   (F)   Road name maps depicting the new road names will be on display for 15
days after completion of all road naming meetings and assignment of all
proposed road names at the following locations:
      (1)   County courthouse;
      (2)   County public library (Pennington Gap); and
      (3)   Rose Hill Community Library.
   (G)   A public hearing will be advertised and held for the approval of the
new road names.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-78 ROAD NAMING REGULATIONS.
   The following road name regulations must be followed when naming roads:
   (A)   Existing, documented road names, if not duplicated elsewhere in the
county, take precedence in every scenario. The Board of Supervisors may suggest
an existing (pre-E-911 addressing and mapping project) road name change if the
current road name does not conform to this chapter;
   (B)   Names must be pleasant sounding, easy to read, non-offensive and add
prestige to the community;
   (C)   Duplicate and/or sound-alike road names are prohibited;
   (D)   The county will assign a road name suffix at their discretion;
residents may not suggest a road name suffix. The following are suffix
definitions.
      (1)   Public county roads (not incorporated):
         (a)   HWY: any federal or state highway;
         (b)   RD: any secondary road;
         (c)   LP: any secondary road that begins and ends on the same road;
and
         (d)   PKWY: special scenic route or park drive.
      (2)   All private, non-incorporated roads: TRL or DR - all named, private
roads.
      (3)   Suggested public incorporated roads: the following are suffix
suggestions for all incorporated roads. The incorporated entity has the
authority to adopt the road name and suffix of their choosing. The county
recommends the incorporated entity use the following guidelines as a mechanism
for standardizing road suffixes throughout the county within incorporated
entities:
         (a)   ST: road that generally, but not always, runs in a north/south
direction;
         (b)   AVE: road that generally, but not always, runs in an east/west
direction;
         (c)   CIR: road that begins and ends on the same road;
         (d)   PL: cul-de-sac or permanent dead-end road; and
         (e)   LN: all name, private roads.
   (E)   Pre- and post- directionals are prohibited. Existing directionals
within incorporated entities may be necessary to prevent duplicate addresses.
Example:
      105 N MAIN ST and 105 S MAIN ST.
   (F)   Numeric digits and spelled-out numbers in conjunction with non-numeric
words are prohibited, except when used with a designator such as st, nd rd, th.
Example:
      TWO HORSE RD is prohibited.
      2ND ST is permissible.
   (G)   Road names may not be more than 20 letters in length. Spaces in multi-
word road names qualify as a letter of length. This excludes the suffix that
will be assigned by the county.
   (H)   Proper, personal names are not permitted, with the exception that
historical or other notable individuals may be honored in naming of a public
road. Non-conforming proper, personal names adopted in the initial road naming
phase shall be allowed to continue (grandfathered). Names of rivers, mountains
and the like are permissible if the name of the river, mountain and the like
has been otherwise officially adopted. Example:
      (1)   POWELL MOUNTAIN RD is permissible;
      (2)   JIM JONES RD is not permissible;
      (3)   JONES RD is not permissible;
      (4)   JIM RD is not permissible; and
      (5)   DANIEL BOONE RD is permissible.
   (I)   Where duplicate road names exist or arise during the road naming
process, the road name shall be given to the road that affects the most number
of addressable structures.
   (J)   Any character besides a letter of the English alphabet or space is
prohibited in a road name (such as, ampersand, hyphen and period).
   (K)   Road names that could possibly also be suffixes or directionals are
prohibited. Example:
      (1)   BENDY ROAD TRL is prohibited; and
      (2)   NORTH RUN RD is prohibited.
   (L)   Fractions are prohibited. Example: 5-1/2 AVE is prohibited.
   (M)   The word “and” is prohibited. Example: LOG AND COAL RD is prohibited.
   (N) A road name suggestion may only be offered by a resident that owns a
parcel adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which has legal access from, the road
for which the suggestion is being made.
   (O)   U.S. and state highways naming procedure:
      (1)   U.S. and state highways will be named;
      (2)   Any U.S. or state highway will have the same name throughout the
entirety of the said U.S. or state highway; and
      (3)   The Board of Supervisors will be responsible for assigning a name
to each U.S. and state highway in the county.
   (P)   (1)   Words in any street name must be spelled out; no abbreviations
are allowed, except for the road name suffix which will be assigned by the
county.
      (2)   Example: BRANCH MTN RD is prohibited.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-79 ROAD NAMING SUGGESTIONS.
   The following road name suggestions should be considered when naming roads:
   (A)   Commonly recognized road names that are not documented, but well
known, should be considered;
   (B)   Historical or geographic characteristics should be considered; and
   (C)   If an area does not have a common name or theme, attempt to identify a
theme for several roads (such as, birds, trees and the like).
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-80 ROAD SEGMENTS.
   Each road shall bear the same name and uniform numbering along the entirety
of the road. Segments of roads shall not be allowed to have different or
separate names.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-81 OFF-SET INTERSECTIONS AND SPLIT ROUTES.
   Split routes, also known as dog-leg of off-set intersections, shall be
treated as separate roads with different names and numbering to preserve the
integrity and continuity of the number system.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-82 IMPASSES.
   Impasses or sections of a road that are impassable shall be assigned
different names and numbering to each portion of the road on either side of the
impasse to preserve the integrity and continuity of the numbering system.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-83 ROAD NAME CHANGE MORATORIUM.
   For the period of time between road name adoption by the Board of
Supervisors and two years after the first, a live enhanced 911 call is received
by the county’s Communications/E-911 Center, no road names adopted during the
road naming process described herein may change by means of public petition.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-84 ROAD NAME CHANGE PETITION.
   After a period of two years after the first, live enhanced 911 call is
received by the county public safety answering point, a citizen or group of
citizens must meet the following criteria and may use the following road name
change petition procedure to petition a road name.
   (A)   A road name change petition may only be offered by a resident that
owns a parcel adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which has legal access from,
the road for which the petition is being made.
   (B)   Roads with less than ten parcels must have a complete parcel owner
consensus in favor of what the proposed road name will be.
   (C)   Roads with ten or more parcels must have at least three-fourths parcel
owner majority in favor of what the proposed road name will be.
   (D)   The petition must contain the names and signatures of all parcel
owners on roads with less than ten parcels or three-fourths of the parcel
owners on roads with ten or more parcels.
   (E)   The petition must be accompanied by a $100 petition submission fee.
   (F)   The petition must include the current road name, up to three proposed
road names, and why the petitioner(s) feels the road name should be changed.
   (G)   The petition will be open for public discussion at a public hearing. A
decision will be made by the Board of Supervisors whether or not to change the
road name.
   (H)   If approval is denied, the Board of Supervisors, or its designee,
shall provide a written statement of the reason(s) for non-approval.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-85 ROAD NAME ADOPTION AFTER THE INITIAL E-911 ROAD NAMING PROCESS.
   (A)   Future roads shall be named when they are:
      (1)   Public;
      (2)   Private and longer than 1,000 feet with one addressable structure
along the road; or
      (3)   Private with three or more addressable structures along the private
road.
   (B)   Any future road shall be named by the following procedure when:
      (1)   (a)   A private road is created or extended to more than 1,000 feet
in length on which only one addressable structure exists;
         (b)   New road naming guidelines:
            1.   The owner of the addressable structure may, within ten
business days after notification by the E-911 Coordinator, submit up to three
road name suggestions to the E-911 Coordinator by mail or in person. The
person’s name should be printed legibly on the suggestion. Failure to provide
suggestions within the time allowed shall authorize the E-911 Coordinator to
assign a random, pleasant sounding, easy to read, non-offensive name to the
road;
            2.   Road name suggestions must comply with this chapter;
            3.   The E-911 Coordinator will assign the road name suffix; and
            4.   No public hearing is necessary; the road name becomes
official.
      (2)   An event has occurred to an existing private unnamed road or public
road that requires readdressing residents.
         (a)   Examples:
            1.   Addition of addressable structures on private road less than
1,000 feet in length so that three or more addressable structures result on the
private road; and
            2.   A public road is re-routed, extended and the like.
         (b)   New road naming guidelines:
            1.   When the new road qualifies for a name, each parcel owner
adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which has legal access from, the new road
may, within ten business days after notification by the E-911 Coordinator,
submit up to three road name suggestions to the E-911 Coordinator by mail or in
person. The persons name should be printed legibly on the suggestion. Failure
to provide suggestions within the time allowed shall authorize the E-911
Coordinator to assign a random, pleasant sounding, easy to read, non-offensive
name to the road;
            2.   Road name suggestions must comply with this chapter;
            3.   The E-911 Coordinator will assign the road name suffix;
            4.   The E-911 Coordinator will select the name deemed most
acceptable from the submitted suggestions;
            5.   The E-911 Coordinator will submit the road name suggestion to
the Board of Supervisors with a letter confirming that the new road name is in
compliance with this chapter;
            6.   The road name becomes official when adopted by the Board of
Supervisors after a duly held public hearing; and
            7.   If each parcel owner adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which
has legal access from, the new road sign, a statement in agreement with the
road name selected by the E-911 Coordinator, subsections (B)(2)(b)5. and (B)(2)
(b)6. above may be omitted and the road name becomes official.
      (3)   (a)   A private auction or land sale will occur which may result in
the split of existing parcels and new roads.
         (b)   New road naming guidelines:
            1.   If a new road is built, it must first either be public,
private more than 1,000 feet in length, or private with three or more
addressable structures’ parcels adjacent to the new road before the new road
qualifies for a name;
            2.   Road names that were never officially previously adopted are
void and subject to change by the county as prescribed in this chapter;
            3.   When the new road qualifies for a name, each parcel owner
adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which has legal access from, the new road
may, within ten business days after notification by the E-911 Coordinator,
submit up to three road name suggestions to the E-911 Coordinator by mail or in
person. The person’s name should be printed legibly on the suggestion. Failure
to provide suggestions within the time allowed shall authorize the E-911
Coordinator to assign a random, pleasant sounding, easy to read, non-offensive
name to the road;
            4.   Road name suggestions must comply with this chapter;
            5.   The E-911 Coordinator will assign the road name suffix;
            6.   The E-911 Coordinator will chose the name deemed most
acceptable from the submitted suggestions;
            7.   The E-911 Coordinator will submit the road name suggestion to
the Board of Supervisors with a letter confirming that the new road name is in
compliance with this chapter;
            8.   The road name becomes official when adopted by the Board of
Supervisors after a duly held public hearing; and
            9.   If each parcel owner adjacent to, or who owns a parcel which
has legal access from, the new road sign a statement in agreement with the road
name selected by the E-911 Coordinator, subsections (B)(3)(b)5. and (B)(3)(b)6.
may be omitted and the road name becomes official.
      (4)   (a)   An official developer’s platted subdivision is being
approved.
         (b)   New road naming procedure:
            1.   Road names considered for adoption must meet the road naming
requirements in this chapter;
            2.   The proposed road names must be approved for compliance with
this chapter by the E-911 Coordinator;
            3.   The E-911 Coordinator will assign the road name suffix;
            4.   A signed letter of compliance of all road names by the E-911
Coordinator must be submitted to the Community Development Director before the
Planning Commission approves the official developer’s platted subdivision
proposal; and
            5.   Road names become official when the platted subdivision map is
approved by the Board of Supervisors after a duly held public hearing.
      (5)   (a)   A new public road is being built on which no addressable
structures exist.
         (b)   New road naming guidelines:
            1.   The Board of Supervisors will assign the name of any new
public road;
            2.   The proposed road name must be approved for compliance with
this chapter by the E-911 Coordinator;
            3.   The E-911 Coordinator will assign the road name suffix;
            4.   A signed letter of compliance of all road names will be
submitted to the Board of Supervisors; and
            5.   The road name(s) become official when adopted by the Board of
Supervisors after a duly held public hearing.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-86—17-94 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VII. AMENDMENTS
§ 17-95 GENERAL.
   The Board of Supervisors may, from time to time, on its own motion or on
petition, after public notice and a hearing as provided by this chapter, amend,
supplement, change, modify or repeal the addressing regulations and
assignments.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-96 PUBLIC NOTIFICATION REQUIREMENTS.
   Before adopting or amending this chapter, the Board of Supervisors shall
conduct a public hearing on the proposal. A notice of the public hearing shall
be advertised once a week for two successive calendar weeks in a newspaper
having general circulation in the area. The notice shall be published for the
first time not less than ten days nor more than 25 days before the appointed
date of the public hearing.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-97 LETTER OF NOTIFICATION.
   (A)   Whenever there is a proposal for a change in the addressing system
involving any portion of an address, the land owner of that parcel’s address as
shown on the county tax listing and the land owners of all the parcels abutting
that parcel as shown on the county tax listing, shall be mailed a notice of the
proposed change in the addressing system.
   (B)   The notice shall be mailed by first class mail to the last address
listed of the land owners according to the county tax abstracts.
   (C)   The person or persons responsible for mailing such notices shall
provide written notification to the Board of Supervisors attesting to the
fulfillment of this task.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-98 PROTESTING A PETITION OR PROPOSAL OF AMENDMENT.
   No protest against any change in, or amendment to, the road naming and
addressing ordinance, regulations, proposals or the addressing system, shall be
valid or effective unless it is in the form of a written petition. The petition
shall bear the names and signatures of the opposing property owners and shall
affirm and state the nature of protest to the proposal.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-99 APPLICATION FOR AMENDMENT.
   Applications for an amendment to this chapter shall be filed with the E-911
Coordinator. The E-911 Coordinator shall be responsible for presenting the
application to the County Board of Supervisors. Each application shall be
signed, be in a duplicated form and shall contain the following:
   (A)   The applicant’s name and address in full;
   (B)   In the case of a text amendment, it shall set forth the new text to be
added and the existing text to be deleted and any other text changes that will
have to be made as a result of the effect on the remaining articles, sections,
definitions, diagrams or attachments; and
   (C)   (1)   If the proposed amendment will change the addressing map book, a
copy of the addressing map book page shall be marked to indicate the impact of
the proposed amendment to the existing map book page and shall be presented
with application for amendment.
      (2)   A public hearing shall be held by the Board of Supervisors before
the adoption of any proposed amendments to this chapter. When the Board of
Supervisors shall have denied any application for the change of a portion or
matter of this chapter, it shall not thereafter accept any other application of
the same change involving that portion or matter of the ordinance until the
expiration of 12 months from the date of such previous denial.
      (3)   Before any action shall be taken on an amendment request, the party
or parties proposing or recommending said amendment shall deposit the required
fee of $50 with the E-911 Coordinator at the time the petition is filed to
cover publication and other miscellaneous cost of said change.
      (4)   Under no condition shall said fee or any part thereof be refunded
for failure of said amendment to be adopted. However, in the event an
application is withdrawn prior to the time it is ordered advertised for hearing
by the E-911 Coordinator, three-fourths of the fee shall be refunded.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-100—17-108 RESERVED.
ARTICLE VIII. LEGAL STATUS PROVISION
§ 17-109 VIOLATIONS; ENFORCEMENT; PENALTIES.
   (A)   The following actions are unlawful.
      (1)   Intentional road name, road name sign, address or address display
sign defamation.
         (a)   For any person to use or display a different address or portion
thereof, except as provided by this chapter;
         (b)   For any person to name or designate the name of any private
road, street, drive, cartway, easement, right-of-way, access area or any other
thoroughfare, except as provided by this chapter;
         (c)   For any person to establish or erect any road sign that is the
same color as the road name sign design(s) adopted by the county; and
         (d)   For any person to intentionally destroy, mar, deface or steal
any county road name sign.
      (2)   Concealment or confusion.
         (a)   To cover or conceal or to permit the sight obstruction of the
structure numbers required to be displayed by this chapter;
         (b)   To post other numbers that would be confusing. All old numbers
on structures shall be removed when the county has assigned a new structure
number; and
         (c)   To provide a structure address to any telephone company, utility
company or government office that has not been identified and approved by
County E-911 as being a valid address in an attempt to obtain telecommunication
or electrical services. Telephone companies serving the county shall verify
with county E-911 the address for any customers attempting to secure
residential or commercial telecommunication services prior to supplying such
service.
   (B)   Any other violations of a requirement of this chapter.
      (1)   Whenever the County Administrator, or his or her duly authorized
agent, has reason to believe there has been or there exists a violation of this
chapter, he or she shall give written notice of such violation to the person
failing to comply, and order said person to take corrective measures within 14
calendar days from the date of the notification. If such person fails to comply
with the duly issued order, the County Administrator, or his or his agent,
shall initiate necessary actions to terminate the violation through criminal
enforcement including but not limited to injunctive relief.
      (2)   Any violation of this chapter shall constitute a Class 4
misdemeanor punishable by a fine of not more than $250. Subsequent to the 14-
calendar day period following notification of violation, each day of violation
shall constitute a separate violation.
      (3)   Nothing herein contained shall prevent the county from taking other
such lawful actions as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation.
      (4)   When enforcing the Uniform Statewide Building Code (USBC), being VA
Code Title 36, Chapter 6, the Building Official and any assistant, has the
authority to enforce the provisions of this chapter.
      (5)   All law enforcement officers in the commonwealth with the authority
to issue state uniform summons shall have authority to enforce this chapter.
      (6)   All fines and penalties levied in violation of this chapter shall
be paid over to the County Treasurer from the General District Court or Circuit
Court, as applicable, and deposited in the county general fund, as provided by
law.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§§ 17-110—17-118 RESERVED.
ARTICLE IX. VIOLATIONS AND ENFORCEMENT
§ 17-119 POSTING REQUIREMENTS VIOLATIONS.
   Failure to comply with the posting requirements of §§
17-63 through 17-75 constitutes a violation of this chapter.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-120 POSTING ADDRESSABLE STRUCTURE NUMBERS.
   Civil penalties may be imposed in accordance with the following procedure:
   (A)   Initial notification of violation, in writing by first class mail, to
last known address of the person to be notified;
   (B)   If not corrected within ten days, a warning citation may be issued;
   (C)   If not corrected within seven days of issuance of a warning citation,
a second citation including a fine of $25 may be issued; and
   (D)   Each day the violation continues shall constitute a separate violation
of this chapter.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-121 NOTIFICATION OF VIOLATION.
   Notification of violation shall:
   (A)   Be issued by the Board of Supervisors or its designee;
   (B)   Be in writing, first class mail directed to the name and address of
the owner of the addressable structure; and
   (C)   Must set forth the action necessary for the offender to be in
compliance with this chapter.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
§ 17-122 LEGAL PROSECUTION.
   Nothing herein contained shall prevent the county from taking other such
lawful actions as is necessary to prevent or remedy any violation.
(Ord. passed 1-20-2015)
CHAPTER 18: WATER CONSERVATION
Section
Article I. In General
   
18-1   Purpose
   
18-2   Declaration of emergency
   
18-3—18-11   Reserved
Article II. Contingency Plans
   
18-12   Advisory level
   
18-13   Contingency Plan No. 1 - mandatory
   
18-14   Contingency Plan No. 2 - severe
   
18-15   Contingency Plan No. 3 - emergency
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
§ 18-1 PURPOSE.
   The purpose of this chapter is to provide planned contingency methods of
limiting the use of water during water shortage situations and to provide the
County Public Service Authority and its water users with notification of the
plan well in advance, so that PSA customers may have opportunity to make their
own contingency plan, and to provide, by ordinance, a means of enforcement of
such actions thereunder.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)
§ 18-2 DECLARATION OF EMERGENCY.
   (A)   (1)   The Director of the County Public Service Authority and the PSA
Engineer will consult with the chairperson of the PSA to determine if a special
called meeting should be called according the by-laws of the PSA, to declare a
water emergency. Upon declaration of a water emergency condition, one of the
categories of contingency plans outlined below will be put in effect. The plan
put in effect will be determined by the seriousness of the emergency condition
declared.
      (2)   The declaration may be within only certain systems operated by the
PSA or within all systems operated by the PSA, as determined by the need. A
water emergency is deemed imminent when the total raw water source for the
system or systems reaches a 60-day supply. In the case where water is provided
to the PSA system or systems by another water purveyor, an emergency shall be
deemed imminent when such water purveyor declares an emergency within their
system.
   (B)   The number of days of supply remaining in the water system or systems
shall be determined by the Director and Engineer, who shall gather all
pertinent facts and report their findings to the PSA Board of Directors.
   (C)   The Director will make notification of the emergency through the media
(radio, television and newspapers) and such other means as are reasonably
calculated to make the public aware of the condition.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)
§§ 18-3—18-11 RESERVED.
ARTICLE II. CONTINGENCY PLANS
§ 18-12 ADVISORY LEVEL.
   Upon the determination that a limited water supply is available, the Public
Service Authority, or, when authorized by said body, the Director thereof, may
disseminate information throughout the waterworks system service area advising
that the water supply has been depressed and requesting customers to
voluntarily reduce water demand through the following actions:
   (A)   Reduce or eliminate the use of city water to wash down sidewalks,
walkways, driveways, parking lots, service station aprons, tennis courts, other
hard surfaced areas, buildings, and structures, except as required for safety
concerns;
   (B)   Reduce the use of PSA water to wash automobiles, trucks, trailers and
any other type of mobile equipment, except in facilities operating with an
alternate water source or with a water recycling system; and
   (C)   Reduce the use of PSA water for watering of shrubbery, trees, lawns,
grass, plants and other vegetation, except when using an alternate water
source, recycled water or a watering container not exceeding three gallons in
capacity. Any such watering should be limited to the hours between 8:00 p.m.
and 10:00 a.m.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)
§ 18-13 CONTINGENCY PLAN NO. 1 - MANDATORY.
   (A)   Upon declaration of the emergency, all car washing, street washing,
watering of lawns, gardens and the like, building or window washing, and
swimming pool operation will be ceased immediately.
   (B)   All commercial, industrial, manufacturing or processing facilities
shall immediately reduce water consumption to 80% of the average monthly water
usage as determined by the previous two billings showing on the PSA water
books. A written plan of operation showing the curtailment shall be immediately
submitted by the facility to the Director upon receipt of notice to do so.
   (C)   Upon declaration of the emergency, a surcharge will be placed on all
water consumption at a rate of $5 per 1,000 gallons above the 2,000 gallons per
month minimum, immediately after the declaration of the emergency. However, the
minimum billing amount of 2,000 gallons of water shall be exempt from said
surcharge. The Director will see that all meters are read as soon as possible
after declaration of emergency and after the emergency is over to provide water
consumption figures for use in billing. Further, at the end of said emergency,
the Director shall see that meters are read in the same order in which they
were read at the beginning of said emergency.
   (D)   Violations of the provisions in Contingency Plan No. 1 shall be a
Class 4 misdemeanor.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)
§ 18-14 CONTINGENCY PLAN NO. 2 - SEVERE.
   When the amount of the raw water source reaches a 30 days’ supply, or in the
case where water is provided to the PSA system or systems by another water
purveyor, such water purveyor declares a Contingency Plan No. 2 emergency
within their system, the following additional limitations are imposed, and each
affected person/business will be notified by certified mail by the Director.
   (A)   Bottling plants, industrial and manufacturing or processing
facilities. Production using PSA supplied water will be strictly limited to 50%
of average monthly water usage as determined by the previous two billings
showing on the PSA water books. A written plan of operation showing operation
schedules necessary to reach this curtailment will be submitted to the Director
upon receipt of notice to do so.
   (B)   Food outlets and restaurants. Hours of operation limited to eight
hours/day and maximum of 40 hours/week. Plan of operating hours will be filed
with the Director.
   (C)   Schools, hospitals and nursing homes. Required to use all disposable
paper goods possible in preparation and serving of all meals. Notice to the
Director is required as pertains to the plan of action taken.
   (D)   Beauty shops, barber shops, health spas, laundries and pet shops.
Hours of operation limited to 32 hours/week maximum. Plan of operating hours
will be filed with the Director to allow checks on operation.
   (E)   Violations.
      (1)   Upon receipt of the notification, the plan of action described
above must be filed within 48 hours. Violation of plan filing deadline will be
closed immediately until plan is submitted.
      (2)   Violation of the provisions in Contingency Plan No. 2 shall be a
Class 3 misdemeanor.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)
§ 18-15 CONTINGENCY PLAN NO. 3 - EMERGENCY.
   (A)   When the amount of raw water source water reaches a 15 days’ supply,
or in the case where water is provided to the PSA system or systems by another
water purveyor, such water purveyor declares a Contingency Plan No. 3 emergency
within their system, the following additional limitations are imposed.
      (1)   Bottling plants, industrial and manufacturing or processing
facilities. Production using town water prohibited.
      (2)   Food outlets and restaurants. Hours of operation limited to four
hours/day and maximum of 20 hours/week. Plan of operating hours will be filed
with the Director to allow checks on operation.
      (3)   Beauty shops, barber shops, health spas, laundries and pet shops.
Hours of operation limited to 16 hours/week maximum. Plan of operating hours
will be filed with the Director to allow checks on operation.
   (B)   Violation of the provisions in Contingency Plan No. 3 shall be a Class
3 misdemeanor.
   (C)   In addition to the foregoing, water service may be suspended to any
person who continues to violate the provisions of such a declaration or any
other regulations promulgated hereunder during a water supply emergency. If
such water service is suspended by operation of this chapter, the person shall
pay a reconnection fee and all outstanding charges before service is restored.
(Ord. passed 11-20-2007)

Section

§ 1-1 ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   The county’s zoning ordinance is hereby adopted by reference as if set out
in full. A copy of the zoning ordinance can be found in the office of the Board
of Supervisors.
(Ord. passed 1-21-2014)
APPENDIX B: SUBDIVISION ORDINANCE
Section
   
1-1   Adopted by reference
§ 1-1 ADOPTED BY REFERENCE.
   The county’s subdivision ordinance is hereby adopted by reference as if set
out in full. A copy of the subdivision ordinance can be found in the office of
the Board of Supervisors.
